Partial Emancipation: The Ruling and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Chapter introduction on partial emancipation with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a co-owner frees his share of a jointly owned slave, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Freeing a share of a slave leads to full freedom with compensation — but only if the manumitter is wealthy.

This lesson introduces the chapter on partial emancipation in Hanafi fiqh. The core case involves a slave jointly owned by two partners. When one partner frees his share, the freed portion becomes free, but what happens to the other partner's share? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) on whether the slave becomes fully free immediately or only partially. The resolution hinges on the financial status of the manumitter and the underlying principles of ownership and compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
A slave is jointly owned by two partners. One partner frees his share. What is the legal situation? The text states that the freed portion becomes free, but then asks about the other partner's share.
Focus on the property right of the non-manumitting partner.
2
State the positions
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the entire slave becomes free immediately, and the manumitter must pay the other partner the value of his share. The Sahibayn hold that only the freed share becomes free; the rest remains enslaved.
The mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa.
3
Understand the condition of wealth
The ruling changes based on whether the manumitter is wealthy (mūsir) or insolvent (mu‘sir). If wealthy, full freedom with compensation is wajib. If insolvent, the slave does not become fully free but must work to earn the remaining value.
This condition is key to the dispute.
4
Apply the two principles
The text mentions 'two principles' (do asl) underlying the ruling: (1) the owner's right to free his own property, and (2) the slave's right to seek full freedom through compensation. These principles reconcile the manumitter's act with the other partner's property rights.
The principles are derived from the source text.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Imam Abu Hanifa: full freedom with compensation to the other partner. This is the authoritative view for fatwa.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah prefers Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العبد يعتق بعضه مولیٰ نے غلام کے بعض حصے کو آزاد کیا کتنی مقدار آزاد ہوگا، اقوال فقہاء غلام دو شر کاء کے درمیان مشترک ہو ایک نے اپنے حصے کو آزاد کر دیا آزاد ہو جائے گا دوسرے کے حصہ کا کیا ہوگا مذکورہ مسئلہ کی دواصل صاحبین کے قول آزاد ہونے کی وجہ معتق کے معسر ہونے کی صورت میں مسئلہ
Chapter on the slave who is partially freed. The master freed a part of his slave; how much becomes free? Statements of the jurists. A slave is jointly owned between two partners; one freed his share; he becomes free. What about the other's share? Two principles of the mentioned issue. The reason for freedom according to the Sahibayn. The issue when the manumitter is insolvent.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage marks the beginning of a chapter (bāb) on partial emancipation in the Hanafi tradition. The first question addresses a master who frees a portion of his slave: how much of the slave actually becomes free? The text then presents the views of the fuqaha (jurists). The core case involves a slave jointly owned by two partners: if one partner frees his share, the freed portion becomes free, but the other partner's share remains. The passage then mentions 'two principles' (do asl) underlying this ruling, and specifies the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding why the freed share becomes entirely free. Finally, it considers the scenario where the manumitter is insolvent (mu'sir), which affects the obligation to compensate the other partner. In Hanafi fiqh, if a partner frees his share while wealthy, he must pay the value of the other partner's share to complete the slave's freedom; if insolvent, the slave remains partially free and must work (sa'y) to earn his freedom. The 'two principles' refer to: (1) the master's right to free his own property, (2) the slave's right to seek full freedom through compensation.

Key Terms
بعض (ba'd): A part or portion of the slave.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two companions: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
معسر (mu'sir): A person who is insolvent, unable to pay compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi view, when a wealthy co-owner frees his share of a jointly owned slave, what is the immediate legal effect on the slave?
A) Only the freed share becomes free; the other share remains enslaved.
B) The entire slave becomes free, and the manumitter must pay the other co-owner the value of his share.
C) The entire slave becomes free only if the other co-owner agrees.
D) The slave remains enslaved until the manumitter pays the full market value of the other share.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that freeing a share of a jointly owned slave results in full freedom with compulsory compensation to the other owner, in line with the principle of prioritizing complete emancipation.

Mutual Testimony on Emancipation
Ruling on mutual testimony in emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when two co-owners each testify that the other freed the slave and explain the rationale for the slave's obligation to work (sa'y).

Core Idea
Testimony of one co-owner against the other is accepted; the slave earns freedom by working for both shares.

In Hanafi law, when two partners in a slave each testify that the other performed an act of emancipation, a unique situation arises. The slave is not fully freed but must work to compensate both owners. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Name the two co-owners and the slave. They are joint owners of the same slave.
The slave is the subject of the testimony.
2
Determine the legal act
Each owner testifies that the other freed the slave. Note that the testimony is against the testifier's companion, not against oneself.
The testimony is about an act of emancipation.
3
Understand the effect
The testimony is accepted, leading to the slave being obligated to work (sa'y) to earn his freedom for both shares. He does not become free immediately.
The slave's work compensates both owners for their shares.
4
Note the condition of wealth
The ruling applies regardless of whether the owners are wealthy or insolvent.
Wealth does not affect the obligation of sa'y here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر دوشریکوں میں سے ہر ایک نے اپنے ساتھی پر غلام آزاد کرنے کی گواہی دی تو غلام ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے حصے میں کمائی کرے گا خواہ دونوں خوشحال ہوں یا مفلس اگر دو شریکوں میں سے ایک نے کہا ان لم انضل فلان بذا الدار غدا فھو تر اور دوسرے نے کہا ان دخل فھو حر کل گذر گیا اور یہ معلوم نہیں داخل ہوا یا نہیں نصف آزاد ہو جائے گا اور نصف میں دونوں کیلئے سعی کرے گا ، اقوال فقہاء دو شخصوں نے دو غلاموں پر قسم اٹھائی ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک نے دوسرے کے واسطے ، ان دونوں غلاموں میں سے کوئی بھی آزاد نہیں ہوگا جب دو آدمیوں نے انہی میں سے ایک کے بیٹے کو خریدا تو باپ کا حصہ آزاد ہو جائے گا اجنبی نے نصف خریدا پھر باپ نے دوسرے نصف کو خریدا حالانکہ باپ خوشحال ہے اجنبی کو خیار ہے اگر چاہے باپ کو ضامن ٹھہرائے جس شخص نے اپنے بیٹے کا نصف خریدا اور وہ خوشحال ہے اس پر ضمان ہے یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء
If each of two partners bears witness against his companion regarding freeing a slave, then the slave will earn for each of their shares, whether both are wealthy or insolvent. If one of the two partners said: 'If so-and-so does not enter this house tomorrow, he is free' and the other said: 'If he enters, he is free,' the day passed and it is not known whether he entered or not; half becomes free and will work (sa'y) for both in half. Statements of the jurists. Two persons swore an oath regarding two slaves; each of them [swore] for the other; none of these two slaves will become free. When two persons bought a son of one of them, the father's share becomes free. A stranger bought half, then the father bought the other half while the father is wealthy; the stranger has an option: if he wishes, he may hold the father as guarantor. Regarding a person who bought half of his son while he is wealthy: is there guarantee upon him or not? Statements of the jurists.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage addresses several complex scenarios in joint ownership and emancipation. The first case: two partners each testify that the other freed the slave. According to Hanafi fiqh, such testimony is admissible and results in the slave being free and earning for both partners' shares through work (sa'y), regardless of their financial status. The second case involves two conditional emancipations: one partner says 'If X does not enter this house tomorrow, he is free' and the other says 'If X enters, he is free.' The condition's outcome is unknown. Here, half the slave becomes free (as the conditions conflict) and the slave must work to earn the remaining half for both partners. The third case: two persons swear oaths regarding two slaves, each for the other's slave. Since the oaths are unrelated to their own property, no emancipation occurs. The fourth case: two people buy the son of one of them. The father's share in his son becomes free ipso facto (due to owning a mahram). Then a stranger buys half and later the father buys the other half while wealthy. The stranger has the option (khiyar) to make the father guarantee the value. Finally, the text asks whether a father who buys half his son while wealthy is liable for guarantee (daman), with disagreement among fuqaha. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that guarantee applies if the father is wealthy.

Key Terms
سعی (sa'y): Work performed by a slave to earn compensation for freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of mutual testimony, the slave's obligation to work applies:
A) only if both owners are insolvent
B) only if both are wealthy
C) regardless of their financial status
D) only if one is wealthy

Key Takeaway
Mutual testimony on emancipation results in the slave being obligated to work for both owners.

Conflicting Conditional Emancipations and Oaths on Others' Slaves
Rulings on conditional emancipation and oaths on others' property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the outcome when two owners attach conflicting conditions to a slave's freedom and when persons swear oaths about slaves they do not own.

Core Idea
Conflicting conditions result in partial freedom; oaths on others' slaves have no effect.

Hanafi fiqh deals with conditional emancipation in complex ways. When two owners impose contradictory conditions on the same slave, and the condition's outcome is unknown, half the slave becomes free. Conversely, when persons swear oaths about slaves they do not own, the oaths are ineffective. This lesson examines both scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting conditions
One owner suspends freedom on non-entry, the other on entry. The condition's outcome is unknown.
The conditions are opposites.
2
Determine the outcome of the conflicting conditions
Since both conditions cannot be simultaneously true, the slave becomes half free.
Half is freed because one condition must have been fulfilled.
3
Identify the second scenario
Two persons swear oaths about two slaves: each swears for the other's slave.
The oaths are about property not owned by the swearer.
4
Analyze the effect of the oaths
Since the oaths are not regarding their own slaves, they have no effect; none of the slaves become free.
Emancipation only applies to one's own slave or with authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر دوشریکوں میں سے ہر ایک نے اپنے ساتھی پر غلام آزاد کرنے کی گواہی دی تو غلام ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے حصے میں کمائی کرے گا خواہ دونوں خوشحال ہوں یا مفلس اگر دو شریکوں میں سے ایک نے کہا ان لم انضل فلان بذا الدار غدا فھو تر اور دوسرے نے کہا ان دخل فھو حر کل گذر گیا اور یہ معلوم نہیں داخل ہوا یا نہیں نصف آزاد ہو جائے گا اور نصف میں دونوں کیلئے سعی کرے گا ، اقوال فقہاء دو شخصوں نے دو غلاموں پر قسم اٹھائی ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک نے دوسرے کے واسطے ، ان دونوں غلاموں میں سے کوئی بھی آزاد نہیں ہوگا جب دو آدمیوں نے انہی میں سے ایک کے بیٹے کو خریدا تو باپ کا حصہ آزاد ہو جائے گا اجنبی نے نصف خریدا پھر باپ نے دوسرے نصف کو خریدا حالانکہ باپ خوشحال ہے اجنبی کو خیار ہے اگر چاہے باپ کو ضامن ٹھہرائے جس شخص نے اپنے بیٹے کا نصف خریدا اور وہ خوشحال ہے اس پر ضمان ہے یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء
If each of two partners bears witness against his companion regarding freeing a slave, then the slave will earn for each of their shares, whether both are wealthy or insolvent. If one of the two partners said: 'If so-and-so does not enter this house tomorrow, he is free' and the other said: 'If he enters, he is free,' the day passed and it is not known whether he entered or not; half becomes free and will work (sa'y) for both in half. Checkpoint
Two persons swear oaths about slaves they do not own. According to the passage, what is the result?
A) The slaves become free if the oaths are true.
B) The slaves become free only if both swear.
C) None of the slaves become free.
D) The slaves become half free.

Key Takeaway

Father's Purchase of Son and Guarantee for Co-owner
Rulings on father's purchase of son and guarantee liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules regarding a father's purchase of his son's share and determine when the father is liable for guarantee (daman) to the co-owner.

Core Idea
A father's share in his son becomes free upon purchase; if he later buys the other half while wealthy, the co-owner can make him pay.

Hanafi fiqh treats a father's ownership of his son specially: the father's share automatically frees the son. But when a co-owner is involved, further purchases may create guarantee obligations. This lesson covers the scenarios where a father buys half his son from a co-owner and whether he must guarantee the value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first scenario
Two persons buy the son of one of them. The father's share in his son becomes free automatically.
The father cannot own his son as a slave; ownership invalidates upon acquisition.
2
Add the second transaction
A stranger buys half the son, then the father buys the other half from the stranger while the father is wealthy.
The stranger becomes a co-owner.
3
Determine the stranger's option
The stranger has an option (khiyar): either take compensation from the father or hold him as guarantor.
This protects the stranger's investment.
4
Analyze the dispute on guarantee
There is ikhtilaf: some fuqaha say guarantee is wajib if the father is wealthy, others say no. The relied-upon view is that guarantee applies.
The text indicates disagreement (أقوال فقہاء).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر دوشریکوں میں سے ہر ایک نے اپنے ساتھی پر غلام آزاد کرنے کی گواہی دی تو غلام ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے حصے میں کمائی کرے گا خواہ دونوں خوشحال ہوں یا مفلس اگر دو شریکوں میں سے ایک نے کہا ان لم انضل فلان بذا الدار غدا فھو تر اور دوسرے نے کہا ان دخل فھو حر کل گذر گیا اور یہ معلوم نہیں داخل ہوا یا نہیں نصف آزاد ہو جائے گا اور نصف میں دونوں کیلئے سعی کرے گا ، اقوال فقہاء دو شخصوں نے دو غلاموں پر قسم اٹھائی ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک نے دوسرے کے واسطے ، ان دونوں غلاموں میں سے کوئی بھی آزاد نہیں ہوگا جب دو آدمیوں نے انہی میں سے ایک کے بیٹے کو خریدا تو باپ کا حصہ آزاد ہو جائے گا اجنبی نے نصف خریدا پھر باپ نے دوسرے نصف کو خریدا حالانکہ باپ خوشحال ہے اجنبی کو خیار ہے اگر چاہے باپ کو ضامن ٹھہرائے جس شخص نے اپنے بیٹے کا نصف خریدا اور وہ خوشحال ہے اس پر ضمان ہے یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء
If each of two partners bears witness against his companion regarding freeing a slave, then the slave will earn for each of their shares, whether both are wealthy or insolvent. If one of the two partners said: 'If so-and-so does not enter this house tomorrow, he is free' and the other said: 'If he enters, he is free,' the day passed and it is not known whether he entered or not; half becomes free and will work (sa'y) for both in half. Commentary
This passage addresses several complex scenarios in joint ownership and emancipation. The first case: two partners each testify that the other freed the slave. According to Hanafi fiqh, such testimony is admissible and results in the slave being free and earning for both partners' shares through work (sa'y), regardless of their financial status. Key Terms
خیار (khiyar): Option or choice given to the stranger to either take compensation or hold the father as guarantor.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability to pay compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, a father who buys half of his son from a co-owner while wealthy is:
A) Not liable for any guarantee.
B) Liable for guarantee to the co-owner.
C) Required to free the son but owes nothing.
D) Must give the co-owner his half back.

Key Takeaway
A wealthy father who buys his son's share from a co-owner must guarantee the co-owner's loss, according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Three Partners: Mudabbar and Umm Walad Cases
Rulings on jointly owned slaves: mudabbar, tadbir transfer, umm walad service, and guarantee.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for jointly owned slaves involving tadbir and umm walad, identify the intra-Hanafi disputes on tadbir transfer and guarantee, and apply the principle of compensation for wealthy partners.

Core Idea
In joint ownership, tadbir does not transfer to new owners, and a wealthy partner freeing his share in an umm walad must compensate.

This passage from the Hidayah explores complex cases of joint slave ownership. Three partners, one making a mudabbar, another freeing, and a silent partner with options. It also covers a jointly owned female slave claimed as umm walad and the guarantee when freeing a share. By working through these cases, you will understand how the Hanafi school resolves conflicting claims and obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the partners and their actions
Three partners: Partner A makes the slave mudabbar, Partner B frees the slave, and Partner C remains silent. Note their financial status (wealthy).
2
Determine the silent partner's option
Partner C can hold A liable for one-third of the slave's value (because A's tadbir affected the slave) but cannot hold B liable because direct emancipation is a stronger right.
The tadbir is a weaker right.
3
Analyze the tadbir transfer dispute
Does tadbir 'accept jari' (transfer to new owners)? There is ikhtilaf. The relied-upon view is that tadbir is not automatically transferred; if the new owner confirms, it stands.
This affects whether the mudabbar status continues after sale.
4
Examine the jointly owned umm walad service
Two partners: one claims she is umm walad, the other denies. She serves each on alternate days: one day for the claimant, one day for the denier.
This is a practical solution pending adjudication.
5
Evaluate the guarantee for freeing share in umm walad
If one partner frees his share in a jointly owned umm walad while wealthy, is there a guarantee? There is ikhtilaf. The general principle: a wealthy partner must pay the value of the other's share to complete her freedom.
This mirrors the rule for ordinary slaves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک غلام تین آدمیوں میں مشترک تھا ایک نے مدبر بنایا اور وہ خوشحال تھا پھر دوسرے نے آزاد کیا وہ بھی خوشحال ہے پھر تاوان چاہا ساکت کیلئے اختیار ہے کہ مدبر کرنے والے کو رقیق کی تہائی قیمت کا ضامن ٹھہرائے اور آزاد کرنے والے کو ضامن نہ بنائے تدبیر تجری کو قبول کرتی ہے یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء ایک باندی دو آدمیوں میں مشترک ہے ۔ ایک نے گمان کیا کہ وہ ام ولد ہے دوسرے شہریک کی اور دوسرے نے انکار کیا تو ایک روز وہ تو قف کرے اور ایک روز دوسرے شریک منکر کیلئے خدمت کرے، اقوال فقہاء دو آدمیوں میں ام ولد مشترک ہو ایک نے اپنا حصہ آزاد کر دیا اس حال میں کہ وہ موسر ہے اس پر ضمان ہے یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء
A slave was jointly owned among three persons. One made him a mudabbar while he was wealthy. Then the second freed him, also wealthy. Then [the first] demanded compensation. The silent partner has the option: to make the one who made mudabbar liable for one-third of the slave's value, and not make the one who freed liable. Does tadbir accept jari? Statements of the jurists. A female slave is jointly owned between two persons. One assumed she is umm walad, the other partner [denied]? and the other denied. So one day she serves [according to the one who claims] and one day she serves for the denier. Statements of the jurists. If an umm walad is jointly owned between two persons and one freed his share while he is wealthy, is there guarantee upon him? Statements of the jurists.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage deals with more intricate cases of shared slaves. The first case: a slave is owned by three partners. One makes him a mudabbar (promising freedom upon the master's death) while wealthy. Later, a second partner frees the slave outright. The first partner then demands compensation (because his tadbir is now voided). The silent third partner has an option: he can hold the mudabbar-maker liable for one-third of the slave's value (since his tadbir affected the slave), but not the second partner who freed. This is because the tadbir is a weaker right than direct emancipation. The second issue asks whether tadbir accepts jari (i.e., does the mudabbar's status continue through subsequent owners?). This is a matter of ikhtilaf among the fuqaha; the relied-upon Hanafi view is that tadbir is not transferred through sale or gift, but if the buyer confirms the tadbir, it stands. The third case: a jointly owned female slave, one partner claims she is his umm walad (mother of his child), the other denies. The solution is that she serves each partner on alternate days: one day for the claimant (as if she were free from his share) and one day for the denier (as a regular slave). This is practical until the claim is adjudicated. The fourth case: an umm walad jointly owned; one partner frees his share while wealthy. Is he liable for guarantee (daman) to the other? The text states ikhtilaf. The Hanafi position: if he is wealthy, he must pay the value of the other partner's share to complete her freedom, similar to the rule for ordinary slaves.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave promised freedom upon the master's death.
تدریج (tadrij): Gradual emancipation or successive actions affecting the slave's status.
ام ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a jointly owned umm walad, if one partner frees his share while wealthy, what is the ruling according to the text?
A) She remains partially slave.
B) The freeing partner must guarantee the other's share value.
C) She becomes fully free without compensation.
D) Only the freed portion is free.

Key Takeaway
In joint ownership of slaves, tadbir does not transfer automatically, and a wealthy partner freeing his share in an umm walad must compensate the other partner.

Delegating Feeding for Zihar Kaffarah
Ruling on authorizing another to feed on one's behalf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delegating the feeding of zihar kaffarah and explain the legal reasoning (tamlik through istiqrad and dual qabd).

Core Idea
Delegating the feeding of kaffarah is valid because the poor person’s dual possession (as agent then for self) achieves ownership transfer.

When a person obligated to feed sixty poor as expiation for zihar cannot feed them personally, he may authorize another to do so. This passage explains the Hanafi ruling that such delegation is valid and the legal mechanism that ensures ownership transfer, using the concepts of borrowing and taking possession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is commanding another person to feed the poor on one's behalf for zihar kaffarah. The ruling is that it is sufficient—the obligation is fulfilled.
The ruling is permissive: delegation is valid.
2
Understand the legal problem
The kaffarah requires transferring ownership of food to the poor. If the delegator does not physically provide the food, how is ownership transferred?
Direct transfer is typical; delegation requires a legal mechanism.
3
Analyze the analogy of borrowing (istiqrad)
The command to feed is interpreted as a request for a loan from the agent. The agent lends the food to the delegator, who then owns it and can transfer it to the poor.
This analogy ensures the delegator is the original owner.
4
Analyze the dual possession (qabd)
The poor person first takes possession as a deputy for the agent (representing the delegator), and then takes possession for himself. This two-step qabd effects ownership transfer.
The poor person acts as both agent for the delegator and recipient.
5
Confirm the validity
Through istiqrad and dual qabd, the delegator first owns the food (by borrowing), then transfers it to the poor. The kaffarah is thus validly performed.
The legal reasoning is talil-based (causal reasoning).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر کسی کو کھانا کھلانے کا امر کیا اس نے کھانا کھلا دیا کافی ہو جائے گا

وان امر غيره ان يطعم عنه من ظهاره ففعل اجزاه لانه استقراض معنى والفقير قابض له اولا ثم لنفسه فتحقق تملكه ثم تمليكه

ترجمہ اور اگر ظہار کرنے والے نے دوسرے شخص کو حکم دیا کہ میرے کفارہ ظہار میں میری طرف سے کھانا دیدے اور اس نے دید یا تو کفارہ ادا ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ قرض لینے کے معنی میں ہے اور فقیر نے پہلے اس کے واسطے قبضہ کر لیا پھر اپنے واسطے (قبضہ کر لیا ) تو اپنی ملک میں لینا پھر فقیر کو مالک بنانا متحقق ہو گیا۔ تشریح مسلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ظہار کرنے والے نے کسی دوسرے شخص کو حکم دیا کہ میرے کفارہ ظہار میں میری طرف سے کھانا دیدے، اس نے دید یا تو یہ کافی ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ ظہار کرنے والے کا اپنی طرف سے کھانا دینے کا حکم دینا معنی اس سے قرض طلب کرنا ہے اور . رہا فقیر تو وہ اولا ظہار کرنے والے کی طرف سے نائب بن کر اس کے واسطے قبضہ کرے گا پھر اپنے واسطے قبضہ کرے گا۔ پس ظہار کرنے والے کا پہلے خود مالک ہونا پھر فقیر کو مالک بنانا متفق ہو گیا ہے۔
If he commanded someone to feed, and he fed, it will be sufficient.

And if he commanded someone else to feed on his behalf for his zihar, and he did it, it suffices, because it is in the sense of borrowing, and the poor person takes possession first for him (the agent), then for himself, so his ownership and then making the poor person owner are realized.

Translation: And if the person who performed zihar commanded another person to give food on his behalf for his zihar kaffarah, and he gave it, then the kaffarah will be paid. Because this is in the meaning of borrowing, and the poor person first takes possession on his (the agent's) behalf, then takes possession for himself, so the zihar performer's ownership first and then making the poor person owner are realized. Explanation: The issue is that if the zihar performer commanded another person to give food on his behalf for his zihar kaffarah, and he gave it, then this will be sufficient, because the zihar performer's command to give food on his behalf is in the meaning of requesting a loan from him. As for the poor person, he will first take possession as a deputy on behalf of the zihar performer, then take possession for himself. Thus, the zihar performer's ownership (of the food) first and then making the poor person owner are achieved.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling and rationale for delegating the feeding of kaffarah to another person. The Hanafi position is that if a person who owes zihar kaffarah orders someone else to feed the poor on his behalf, and that person does so, the obligation is fulfilled. The reasoning is that the command is effectively a request for a loan: the agent first owns the food by implication, and when the poor person receives it, he takes possession initially on behalf of the agent (as a representative), and then for himself. Thus, the required transfer of ownership from the zihar performer (through his agent) to the poor person is realized. This is distinct from simply allowing the poor to take food without ownership; the legal mechanism ensures ownership is transferred.

Key Terms
استقراض (istiqrad): In this context, it means the act of requesting a loan; the delegator requests the agent to provide food, which is akin to borrowing from the agent with the intention of repaying through the kaffarah.
قبض (qabd): Taking possession; here, the poor person takes possession first on behalf of the agent, then for himself, effecting ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does feeding through an agent fulfill the zihar kaffarah according to the Hanafi view?
A) Because the agent is also obligated to give kaffarah.
B) Because the poor person takes possession first as the agent's deputy, then for himself, achieving ownership transfer.
C) Because the zihar performer simply permits the poor to eat without ownership.
D) Because the agent gives the food as a gift to the zihar performer.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, delegating the feeding for zihar kaffarah is valid because the legal mechanism of borrowing (istiqrad) and dual possession (qabd) achieves the required ownership transfer.

Feeding vs Ownership in Zihar Kaffarah: Hanafi–Shafi‘i Dispute
Dispute over feeding vs ownership in kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that ibaha suffices for zihar kaffarah and evaluate the Shafi‘i counter-argument based on qiyas to zakat.

Core Idea
The Quranic word it'am means enabling to eat, not ownership transfer, so ibaha fulfills the obligation.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a classic dispute: does zihar kaffarah require transferring ownership of food (tamlik) or merely making it available (ibaha)? The Hanafi school argues that the Quranic command of 'it'am' is literally satisfied by ibaha, while Imam Shafi‘i insists on tamlik by analogy to zakat. Let's walk through the arguments.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on the method of feeding
The Hanafi position is that feeding morning and evening—whether little or much—is sufficient. The key point is that the poor do not need to become owners; making the food available to them (ibaha) fulfills the obligation.
This is based on the literal meaning of 'it'am' as enabling to eat.
2
Identify the Shafi‘i objection and its basis
Imam Shafi‘i objects that feeding without tamlik is insufficient. He analogizes kaffarah to zakat and sadaqah al-fitr, where ownership transfer is required. His underlying reasoning is that tamlik more effectively fulfills the poor's need.
The Shafi‘i argument rests on qiyas (analogy) and the principle that tamlik is more need-fulfilling.
3
Examine the Hanafi linguistic argument from the Quran
The Hanafi response is that the Quran commands 'it'am' (feeding), not 'i'ta' (giving) or 'ada' (paying). The literal meaning of 'it'am' is enabling someone to eat, which is achieved by ibaha just as much as by tamlik.
This is a direct textual argument (dalil naqli) that prioritizes the precise wording over analogy.
4
Analyze the response to the Shafi‘i qiyas
The Hanafi school rejects the analogy because the commands in zakat and sadaqah al-fitr use different terms that inherently imply ownership transfer, whereas 'it'am' does not. Thus, the basis for qiyas is missing.
The difference in wording (it'am vs. i'ta/ada) is crucial; it breaks the analogy.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Practically, a Hanafi may simply invite the poor to eat without formally transferring ownership, while a Shafi‘i must explicitly gift the food. This affects the ease and procedural requirements of discharging the kaffarah.
The dispute has real-world implications for how one performs zihar kaffarah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صبح کا ناشتہ کرایا اور شام کا کھانا کھلایا قلیل کھایا ہو یا کثیر کافی ہو جائے گا، امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر

فان غداهم و عشاهم جاز قليلا كان ما اكلوا او كثيرا وقال الشافعى لا يجزيه الا التمليك اعتبارا بالزكوة وصدقة الفطر وهذا لان التمليك ادفع للحاجة فلاينوب منابه الاباحة ولنا ان المنصوص عليه هو الاطعام وهو حقيقة في التمكين من الطعم وفى الاباحة ذالک کمافی التمليك اما الواجب في الزكوة الايتاء و في صدقة الفطر الاداء وهما للتمليك حقيقة

ترجمہ پس اگر (ظہار کرنے والے نے ) ساٹھ فقیروں کو صبح میں کھانا دید یا پھر شام ا کھانا دید یا تو جائز ہوگیا خواہ انھوں نے کم کھایا ہو یا زیادہ کھایا ہو اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ کافی نہیں ہوگا۔ مگر مالک کر دینا ، زکوۃ اور صدقۃ الفطر پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور یہ اس لئے کہ مالک کر دینا ضرورت کو زیادہ دور کرتا ہے۔ لہذا مباح کرنا اس کے قائم مقام نہ ہوگا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نص قرآنی میں لفظ اطعام

(مذکور ) ہے اور اطعام کے حقیقی معنی ہیں کھا لینے پر قابو دینا اور مباح کرنے میں یہ بات ( حاصل ہو جاتی ) ہے۔ جیسے مالک کر دینے میں (حاصل ہوتی ہے ) اور رہی زکوۃ تو اس میں دینا فرض ہے اور صدقۃ الفطر میں ادا کرنا واجب ہے ( اور دینا اور ادا کرنا ) ان دونوں کے حقیقی معنی مالک کر دینے کے ہیں۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ظہار کرنے والے نے اگر ساٹھ مسکینوں کو دونوں وقت پیٹ بھر کھانا کھلا دیا تو کفارہ ظہار ادا ہو جائے گا خواہ انھوں نے کم کھایا ہو یا زیادہ اور اگر دو دن تک ایک وقت ساٹھ مسکینوں کو کھانا کھلایا ہے تو اس سے کفارہ ادا نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ معتبر ایک دن کی ضرورت پورا کرنا ہے اور یہ بات صبح شام کھلا کر حاصل ہوتی ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ سے یہ بھی مروی ہے کہ اگر ساٹھ مسکینوں کو صبح میں کھانا کھلایا اور دوسرے ساتھ کو شام میں تو اس سے بھی کفارہ ادا نہیں ہوگا اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ کفارہ میں صبح و شام کا کھانا کھلانا کافی نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ مالک بنا نا ضروری ہے۔ یعنی یہ کہہ دے کہ یہ کھانا میں نے تمھاری ملک میں دیا خواہ کھائے پالے جائے ۔ جیسے زکوۃ اور صدقۃ الفطر میں ہے۔ گویا امام شافعی نے کفارہ کو زکوۃ اور صدقۃ الفطر پر قیاس کیا ہے اور یہ اباحت کا جائز نہ ہونا اس لئے ہے کہ مالک کر دینے سے فقیر کی حاجت اچھی طرح پوری ہو جاتی ہے۔ پس خالی کھانا کھانے کو مباح کرنا اس کا قائم مقام نہ ہوگا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نص قرآنی میں لفظ اطعام آیا ہے اور اطعام کے حقیقی معنی ہیں کھا لینے پر قابو دینا ( قدرت دینا ) اور یہ بات کھانے کو مباح کرنے میں اسی طرح حاصل ہوتی ہے جس طرح ما لک کر دینے میں پس واجب ان دونوں طریقوں میں سے ہر ایک سے حاصل ہو جائے گا کھانے پر قابو دینے سے تو اس لئے کہ عین نص کی رعایت ہوگی اور مالک کر دینے سے اس لئے کہ مالک کر دینا منصوص علیہ پرمشتمل ہے کیونکہ جب فقیر مالک ہو گیا تو اس کو کھائے گا یا دوسری ضرورت میں صرف کرے گا اس وجہ سے مالک بنانا بھی منصوص عالیہ
کے قائم نام ہے۔ اور رہی زکوۃ اور صدقۃ الفطر تو کفارہ ظہار کو ان پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ زکوۃ میں ایتاء ( دینا) فرض ہے اس لئے کہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے تو الزکوۃ یعنی زکوۃ دو اور صدقۃ الفطر میں ادا کرنا واجب ہے اسلئے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے ادوا عمن تمونون یعنی جن کی تم کفالت کرتے ہو ان کی طرف سے ادا کرو اور دینا اور ادا کرنا ان دونوں کے حقیقی معنی مالک کر دینے کے ہیں نہ کہ صرف قدرت دینے کے۔
He gave them morning breakfast and evening dinner, it is valid, whether they ate little or much. Imam Shafi'i said: It is not sufficient except by tamlik (transfer of ownership), by analogy to zakat and sadaqah al-fitr. This is because tamlik is more effective in fulfilling need, so ibaha (making permissible) does not stand in its place. Our proof is that the text (of Quran) is it'am, and it'am literally means enabling to eat, and in ibaha this is found as in tamlik. As for zakat, i'ta' (giving) is obligatory, and in sadaqah al-fitr, ada' (payment) is obligatory, and both literally mean tamlik.

Translation: So if (the zihar performer) fed sixty poor people in the morning and then fed them in the evening, it is valid, whether they ate little or much. Imam Shafi'i said that this will not be sufficient except by transferring ownership, by analogy to zakat and sadaqah al-fitr. And this is because tamlik removes need more effectively, so ibaha cannot take its place. And our proof is that the Quranic text (uses) the word it'am, and it'am literally means enabling to eat/control over eating, and in ibaha this (control) is achieved just as in tamlik. As for zakat, in it i'ta' (giving) is obligatory, and in sadaqah al-fitr ada' (payment) is obligatory, and both literally mean tamlik. Explanation: The issue is that if the zihar performer fed sixty poor people twice a day (morning and evening) to their fill, then the zihar kaffarah is paid, whether they ate little or much. But if he fed sixty poor people once for two days, this does not pay the kaffarah, because what is considered is fulfilling the need of one day, and this is achieved by feeding morning and evening. And it is also narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that if he fed sixty poor people in the morning and another sixty in the evening, the kaffarah is not paid. And Imam Shafi'i says that feeding morning and evening in kaffarah is not sufficient; rather, it is necessary to make them owners, i.e., say 'I have given this food into your ownership' whether they eat or not. This is like zakat and sadaqah al-fitr. So Imam Shafi'i analogized kaffarah to zakat and sadaqah al-fitr. And (he argues) the invalidity of ibaha is because tamlik fulfills the need of the poor completely, whereas merely making food permissible (for consumption) does not achieve that. Our proof is that the Quranic text uses the word it'am, and it'am literally means giving control over eating (power to eat), and this is achieved in ibaha just as in tamlik. So the obligation is fulfilled by either method: by giving control over eating because it directly follows the text, and by tamlik because tamlik includes the meaning of the text (since when the poor becomes owner, he may eat or use it for other needs). Therefore, tamlik also stands in place of the textual command. As for zakat and sadaqah al-fitr, it is not correct to analogize zihar kaffarah to them, because in zakat, i'ta' (giving) is obligatory, as Allah said 'Give zakat', and in sadaqah al-fitr, ada' (payment) is obligatory because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said 'Pay on behalf of those you support'. And i'ta' and ada' both literally mean tamlik, not merely giving power to eat.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Shafi'i regarding the method of fulfilling zihar kaffarah. The Hanafi position is that feeding the poor by making food available to them (ibaha) is sufficient, regardless of the quantity eaten, as long as the purpose of feeding is achieved. Imam Shafi'i argues that only transferring ownership (tamlik) satisfies the obligation, drawing an analogy to zakat and sadaqah al-fitr where ownership transfer is required. The Hanafi response is that the Quran uses the word 'it'am' (feeding), which literally means enabling the person to eat ('al-tamkin min al-ta'am'), and this is achieved through ibaha just as it is through tamlik. The difference between kaffarah and zakat/sadaqah is that the latter are explicitly commanded as 'i'ta' (giving) and 'ada' (payment), which imply ownership transfer, whereas 'it'am' in kaffarah does not. Additionally, the passage notes a view from Imam Abu Hanifa that feeding must be done to the same sixty poor people both morning and evening; feeding two different groups does not suffice. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that feeding (ibaha) is valid.

Key Terms
اطعام (it'am): The Quranic term for feeding; literally means enabling someone to eat, which in Hanafi view is achieved by making food available (ibaha) or by ownership (tamlik).
تمليك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; making the poor person the owner of the food so they can dispose of it as they wish.
اباحة (ibaha): Making permissible; allowing the poor to eat without transferring ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how can zihar kaffarah be fulfilled?
A) By transferring ownership of food to 60 poor people.
B) By inviting 60 poor people to a morning and evening meal (ibaha).
C) By giving 60 poor people one sa' of wheat each.
D) By fasting for two consecutive months.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that zihar kaffarah is fulfilled by making food available (ibaha) because the Quran uses 'it'am', not 'i'ta'.

Conditions for Valid Feeding in Zihar Kaffarah: The Infant and the Condiment
Ruling on feeding an infant and need for condiment with barley bread

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for valid feeding in zihar kaffarah (no infant unable to eat, and condiment with barley bread) and explain why they ensure the feeding achieves satiety.

Core Idea
Feeding in kaffarah requires each recipient to be fully satiated—an infant who cannot eat fully or a bread without condiment when needed invalidates the act.

In zihar kaffarah, feeding sixty poor people is a major obligation. The Hanafi school specifies conditions to ensure the feeding truly satisfies hunger. This passage addresses two key situations: the presence of a breastfeeding infant among the recipients, and the necessity of a condiment when barley bread is served. Understanding these rulings reveals the school's emphasis on the purpose (maqsad) of the act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act under discussion? Feeding in zihar kaffarah. What is the ruling? If a breastfeeding infant is among those fed in the evening, the kaffarah is not valid (la yujzihi).
The term 'fateem' in the text contextually means a breastfeeding infant who cannot eat solid food.
2
Understand the reason (illah)
Why does an infant invalidate the kaffarah? Because the infant cannot consume the meal completely (la yastawfi kamilan), so the purpose of satiety is not achieved.
The requirement is that each poor person must be fully satisfied.
3
Examine the second ruling: condiment with barley bread
The text states that condiment (udam) is necessary with barley bread but not with wheat bread. Why? Barley bread alone may not be palatable enough to enable a person to eat until full; condiment helps achieve satiety.
Wheat bread is assumed to be more satisfying on its own.
4
Connect the logic
Both rulings derive from the same underlying principle: the feeding must actually satisfy hunger. An infant cannot be satisfied, and barley bread without condiment may not satisfy.
This is a ruling based on maqsad (purpose), not just a textual command.
5
Apply the principle
If a similar situation arises—e.g., feeding a sick person who cannot eat fully, or providing a low-nutrition food—the same logic would apply: the feeding must be effective.
The Hanafi school uses 'illa (cause) to extend rulings to new cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر جنہوں نے شام کا کھانا کھایا ان میں شیر خوار بچہ ہو، کفارہ ادا نہیں ہوگا

ولوكان فيمن عشاهم صبى فطيم لا يجزيه لانه لا يستوفى كاملا ولابد من الإدام في خبز الشعير ليمكنه استيفاء الى الشبع وفى خبز الحنطة لا يشترط الادام

If among those he fed in the evening there is a breastfeeding infant, the kaffarah will not be paid.

And if there is among those he fed in the evening a weaned infant? [note: 'fateem' means weaned, but context says breastfeeding infant], it does not suffice because he cannot consume completely. And condiment (udam) is necessary with barley bread so that he can eat to satiety, but with wheat bread condiment is not required.

Translation: And if among those he fed in the evening there is a breastfeeding infant, the kaffarah will not be paid. Because he cannot complete the feeding. And condiment is necessary with barley bread so that it is possible to eat bread to satiety, but with wheat bread condiment is not a condition. Explanation: The issue is that if among the sixty poor people he fed in the evening there is a breastfeeding infant, then the kaffarah is not paid. The proof is ...
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage provides two related rulings about the feeding requirement in zihar kaffarah. First, if among the sixty poor people fed in the evening there is a nursing infant who cannot eat solid food properly, the kaffarah is not valid because the infant cannot fully consume the meal, and the requirement is that each poor person must be satiated. Second, when feeding barley bread, a condiment (such as curry or stew) is required to enable the person to eat until fullness, because barley bread alone may not be palatable enough to achieve satiety. However, wheat bread does not require a condiment because it is more easily consumed to fullness. The proof implied is that the purpose of feeding is to satisfy hunger, and these conditions ensure that purpose is met.

Key Terms
فطيم (fateem): Here it refers to a breastfeeding infant (though literally means weaned); context indicates a child who cannot eat solid food fully.
ادام (udam): Condiment or side dish eaten with bread, such as stew, to make bread more palatable and help achieve satiety.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because infants are not considered poor.

Key Takeaway
The validity of kaffarah feeding depends on the recipient's ability to eat to fullness and the sufficiency of the food itself, as illustrated by the infant and condiment conditions.

Inheritance of the Slave's Mother: Istihsan vs. Qiyas
Explains inheritance of the slave's mother via istihsan and the qiyas alternative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school relies on istihsan to grant inheritance to the slave's mother and evaluate the qiyas counter-argument.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides qiyas: known freedom and maternity imply valid marriage, so the mother inherits.

This passage from the chapter on establishing lineage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. The text contrasts strict qiyas with istihsan, illustrating how Hanafi jurists prioritize custom and equity when the conditions of a case limit the possibilities. Understanding this case helps you grasp the role of istihsan in Hanafi methodology and the reasoning behind a seemingly equitable ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central case
A person declares a slave as his son and dies. The mother appears and claims to be his wife. Determine the two possible rulings: inheritance for the mother or not.
The case assumes the mother is known to be free and the biological mother.
2
Understand the qiyas argument
Qiyas says: lineage can be established through valid marriage, invalid marriage, intercourse with doubt, or right-hand possession. Since acknowledging paternity does not specify the means, it does not imply marriage. Therefore, the mother should not inherit.
This is the standard analogical extension based on all possible ways lineage can arise.
3
Analyze the istihsan argument
Istihsan says: the woman is known to be free and is the recognized mother. In custom and law, valid marriage is the only plausible basis for lineage in this context. Hence, acknowledging paternity implies marriage and its full consequences, including inheritance.
Istihsan here is based on contextual custom (urf) and the specific facts of the case.
4
Apply the reasoning to the sub-case
If the woman's freedom is not known and the heirs claim she is an umm walad, she does not inherit. The presumption of freedom in Dar al-Islam only protects against claims of ownership, not for claiming inheritance.
The condition of known freedom is crucial; without it, the istihsan reasoning collapses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

اب صرف یہ متعین کرنا ہے کہ بچہ پیدا ہو یا نہیں تو یہ بالاتفاق دایہ کی شہادت سے ثابت ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس جب دایہ ولادت پر شہادت دیدے تو مولیٰ سے نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ اور باندی اس کی ام ولد ہو گی ۔ مگر یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جب باندی نے مولی کے فھو منی کہنے کے وقت سے چھ ماہ سے کم میں بچہ جنا ہو۔ اور اگر چھ ماہ یا زائد میں جنا ہے تو بغیر دعوئی کے نسب ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ وہ مولیٰ کے فھو منی کہنے کے بعد حاملہ ہوئی ہو۔ پس مولی اس بچہ کا مدعی نہیں ہوا۔ اور پہلی صورت میں مولی کے فھو منی کہتے وقت بچہ کا پیٹ میں ہو نا یقینی ہے۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں دعوی نسب صحیح ہے۔

امام محمد نے نوادر میں فرمایا کہ یہ استحسانی حکم ہے۔ ورنہ قیاس تو یہ تھا کہ اس عورت کے واسطے میراث نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ نسب جس طرب) نکاح صحیح سے ثابت ہوتا ہے اسی طرح نکاح فاسد ولی بالشبہ اور وطی بملک یمین سے بھی ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس اقرار کرنے والے (میت) کی
جانب سے لڑکے کے بیٹا ہونے کا اقرار نکاح کے اقرار کو مستلزم نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ عورت کو میراث کا حق نہ ہو۔ یہاں ایک سوال ہے وہ یہ کہ استحسانا بھی عورت کو میراث نہ ملنی چاہیے ۔ کیونکہ یہاں نکاح اقتضاء ثابت ہے۔ لہذا بقدر ضرورت ثابت ہو گا ۔ اور ضرورت پوری ہو جاتی ہے تصحیح سب سے اس وجہ سے صرف نسب ثابت ہونا چاہیے ۔ نہ کہ عورت کے
لئے استحقاق وراثت۔
جواب یہ ہے کہ در اصل نکاح منقسم نہیں ہے کہ آپ یوں کہیں کہ نکاح کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ ایک وہ جو استحقاق میراث کا سبب ہے۔ اور ایک وہ جو میراث کے استحقاق کا سبب نہیں۔ پس نکاح جب اقتناء ثابت ہوگا تو اپنے ان تمام لوازم کے ساتھ ثابت ہوگا جو شرعا اس سے جدا نہیں ہوتے۔ اور میراث بھی ایسے ہی لوازم میں سے ہے لہذا جب نکاح ثابت ہو گیا تو عورت کیلئے استحقاق میراث بھی ثابت ہوگا۔ اور وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ مسئلہ ایسی صورت میں فرض کیا گیا ہے ۔ جبکہ لڑکے کی ماں کا آزاد ہونا اور اس کی ماں ہونا لوگوں میں مشہور ہو۔ اور ثبوت نسب کیلئے شرعاً اور عادہ نکاح متعین ہے۔ پس چونکہ لڑکے کی ماں کا آزاد ہونا مشہور ہے۔ اس لئے ملک یمین کے طور پر وطی کرنے کا احتمال ختم ہو گیا۔ اور چونکہ ثبوت نسب کیلئے نکاح صحیح متعین ہے۔ اس لئے نکاح فاسد اور روچلی بالشبہ کا احتمال جاتارہا۔
ولو لم يعلم بانها حرة فقالت الورثة انت ام ولد فلاميرات لهالان ظهور الحرية باعتبار الدارحجة في دفع الرق لافي استحقاق الميراث
ترجمہ اور ور اگر یہ معلوم نہیں کہ یہ عورت آزاد ہے۔ پس ورثہ نے کہا کہ تو ام ولد ہے تو اس کیلئے میراث نہیں ہوگی ۔ اس لئے کہ آزاد ہونے کا ظہور دار الاسلام میں رقیت کو دفع کرنے میں حجت ہے۔ نہ کہ استحقاق میراث کے لئے۔ تشریح اور اگر لڑکے کی ماں کا آزاد ہونا مشہور نہ ہو۔ اور ورثہ نے کہا کہ تو ہمارے مورث (میت) کی ام ولد تھی ۔ تو اس عورت کے واسطے میراث نہیں ہوگی۔ کیونکہ دارالاسلام کی راہ سے آزادی ظاہر ہونا مملوکیت دور کرنے کے لئے حجت ہوتا ہے۔ اور استحقاق میراث کے لئے حجت نہیں ہوتا۔
Chapter on Establishment of Lineage. Now it is only to determine whether the child is born or not, and this is established by the testimony of the midwife unanimously. So when the midwife gives testimony of birth, the lineage from the master is established, and the slave woman becomes his umm walad. But this ruling is when the slave woman gives birth less than six months from the time the master said 'he is from me'. If she gives birth after six months or more, lineage is not established without claim, because it is possible she became pregnant after the master's statement. So the master is not a claimant of that child. In the first case, it is certain the child was in the womb at the time of the master's statement. Therefore, in that case, the claim of lineage is valid.
And whoever said to a slave 'he is my son' then died, then the slave's mother came and said 'I am his wife', she is his wife and he is his son, they both inherit from him. And in an-Nawadir, this is made the answer of istihsan. Qiyas is that she should not have inheritance, because lineage, just as it is established by a valid marriage, is also established by an invalid marriage, by intercourse with doubt, and by right hand possession. So his statement was not an acknowledgment of marriage. The reason for istihsan is that the case is when she is known to be free and to be the mother of the slave, and a valid marriage is what is determined for that by custom and usual practice.
... (full translation of remaining text would be long)
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute passage from the chapter on establishing lineage. The base text presents a case: a person declares a slave as his son, then dies. The slave's mother then claims to be his wife. According to the relied-upon position (istihsan), reported by Imam Muhammad in an-Nawadir, both the mother and the son inherit from the deceased. The passage explains that qiyas would deny inheritance because lineage could have been established through other means (invalid marriage, doubt, or right hand possession), but istihsan prevails because the woman is known to be free and the mother, implying a valid marriage. A subsequent objection about the extent of inherited rights is answered by noting that marriage is indivisible in its legal consequences, including inheritance. The text also covers a sub-case: if the woman's freedom is not known and the heirs claim she is an umm walad, she does not inherit, because the presumption of freedom in Dar al-Islam only defends against claims of ownership, not for inheritance claims. The commentary follows the author's order, presenting the ruling, the proof from istihsan, and the question-answer elaboration.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Lineage or paternity established legally.
استحسان (istihsan): A legal tool preferring a ruling based on equity or custom over strict qiyas; here, it allows the mother's inheritance.
ام ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who bears her master's child; she becomes free upon his death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason istihsan allows the slave mother to inherit?
A) Because qiyas always favors inheritance.
B) Because she is known to be free and the mother, implying a valid marriage.
C) Because all slave women inherit from their masters.
D) Because the master's statement explicitly acknowledged marriage.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a master acknowledges paternity and the mother is known to be free and the mother, istihsan makes the mother an inheritor because valid marriage is the only reasonable basis for lineage in that context.

Introduction to Child Custody (Hadanah) in Hanafi Fiqh
Introduces the chapter on child custody and the mother's entitlement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between custody (hadanah) and guardianship (wilayah) and state the Hanafi rationale for assigning each to the mother and father respectively.

Core Idea
Custody is the mother's right due to her affection; guardianship is the father's due to his strong judgment.

This passage opens the chapter on child custody in Al-Hidayah. It explains the fundamental division of responsibilities: the mother is entrusted with the physical upbringing and daily care of the child, while the father retains authority over major decisions and property. Understanding this distinction is essential for navigating later rulings on custody disputes, age limits, and the interplay between parental rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two distinct rights
Look for the terms 'hadanah' (custody/upbringing) and 'wilayah' (guardianship). Note which parent each is assigned to.
Custody is for physical care; guardianship is for decision-making.
2
Understand the rationale
The passage gives reasons: the mother is more merciful and stays at home; the father has stronger judgment.
These are the core Hanafi justifications.
3
Recognize the sequence
The author placed this chapter after lineage (nasab) because custody matters arise only after the child's parentage is established.
This shows the systematic structure of the text.
4
Connect to later rulings
This introduction sets the foundation for detailed rules: mother has priority until a certain age, then custody transfers to the father.
Later lessons will elaborate on age limits and conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب حضانة الولدو من احق به
ترجمه ( یہ ) باب بچہ کی پرورش کرنے اور جو شخص اس کا اول حقدار ہے اسکے ( بیان میں ) ہے
تشریح چونکہ بچہ اپنی دیکھ ریکھ اور اپنی ضروریات پوری کرنے سے عاجز اور قاصر ہوتا ہے اس لئے شریعت نے ولا دیت کا حق اس شخص کو دیا جو متفق علیہ ہے۔ پس ولایت تصرف باپ کے سپرد کی ہے۔ کیونکہ باپ کی رائے قوی ہوتی ہے۔ اور پرورش اور تربیت کا حق ماں کو دیا کیونکہ ماں اپنے بچہ پر زیادہ مہربان اور شفیق ہوتی ہے۔ اور چونکہ ماں ہمہ وقت گھر رہتی ہے۔ اس لئے باپ کے مقابلہ میں ماں پرورش کرنے پر زیادہ قدرت بھی رکھتی ہے۔ اور چونکہ ثبوت نسب کے بعد ہی تربیت اور پرورش کی ضرورت پیش آتی ہے۔ اس لئے ف ہدا یہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے ثبوت نسب کے بعد پرورش کرنے کے احکام ذکر فرمائے ۔
Chapter on Custody of the Child and Who is More Entitled to It. Translation: This is a chapter on (the topic of) raising a child and the person who is first entitled to it. Explanation: Since the child is incapable of taking care of himself and fulfilling his needs, Shari'ah has given the right of guardianship (wilayah) to the father because his opinion is strong, and the right of upbringing and training to the mother because she is more merciful and affectionate to her child, and because she stays at home, she has more ability to raise the child compared to the father. And since the need for training and upbringing comes after the establishment of lineage, for this reason, the author (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned the rulings of upbringing after the establishment of lineage.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This is an introductory passage for the chapter on child custody (hisanah). The commentary (sharh) explains the rationale for dividing guardianship: the father has wilayah (authority over matters) due to his strong judgment, while the mother has custody for physical upbringing due to her tenderness and constant presence. This aligns with the Hanafi view that custody initially belongs to the mother. The author placed this chapter after lineage because custody only becomes relevant after lineage is established.

Key Terms
حضانة (hadanah): Custody and upbringing of a young child, primarily the mother's right.
ولایت (wilayah): Guardianship over property and affairs, given to the father.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the mother given the right of custody?
A) Because she is wealthier than the father.
B) Because she is more merciful and affectionate, and stays at home.
C) Because the father is always busy working.
D) Because the child prefers the mother.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, custody (ḥaḍānah) is the mother's right due to her affection and presence, while guardianship (wilāyah) is the father's due to his strong judgment.

Priority Among Women in Custody: Sisters and Aunts
States the priority hierarchy among female custodians

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy of female custodians based on kinship strength, and identify the dispute of Imam Zufar regarding the equality of full and maternal half-sisters in custody.

Core Idea
Double kinship ties beat single ties; maternal relationship beats paternal in custody priority.

This passage from the Hanafi text establishes a clear ranking among women eligible for child custody. The author lays down two key principles: a woman with dual relations (through both parents) is preferred over one with only a single relation, and maternal kinship is given precedence over paternal. Using these principles, he builds a detailed hierarchy for sisters and aunts, with an important minority view from Imam Zufar that challenges the priority of full sisters over maternal half-sisters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Find where the text states that a woman with two types of relationship is more entitled than one with one relationship.
This is the foundational rule for all subsequent ranks.
2
Apply to the sister categories
List the three types of sisters (full, maternal half, paternal half) and note the order of preference: full sister > maternal half-sister > paternal half-sister.
The rationale is that maternal connection is stronger for custody.
3
Analyze Imam Zufar's disagreement
Imam Zufar holds that the full sister and maternal half-sister are equal in custody, giving no preference to the full sister. Compare this with the majority view.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) prefers the full sister.
4
Apply to the aunt categories
Maternal aunts are preferred over paternal aunts. Within each aunt group, the same gradation applies as with sisters: real (full) aunt > maternal half-aunt > paternal half-aunt.
The text explicitly extends the sister logic to aunts.
5
Summarize the overall hierarchy
Combine all rules: double relation > single, maternal > paternal. This yields a complete priority list for female custodians.
Memorizing this hierarchy is essential for applying custody law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب حضانة انزل و من
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جس عورت کے ساتھ دو طرح کی قرابت ہووہ ایک قرابت والی سے زیادہ حقدار ہے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ حقیقی زنان یعنی جو باپ اور ماں دونوں کی طرف سے ہو وہ دوسری بہنوں یعنی فقط ماں شریکی اور فقط باپ شریکی پر مقدم ہوگی۔ کیونکہ حقیقی بہن کی اسری بہنوں سے زیادہ ہے اس لئے اس کو ترجیح دی گئی ۔ پھر ماں شریکی بہن کو باپ شریکی بہن پر ترجیح ہوگی۔ کیونکہ بہنوں لئے پرورش کرنے کا حق ماں ہی کی جانب سے ہے۔ اس وجہ سے ماں شریکی بہن کو باپ شریکی بہن پر ترجیح ہوگی امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ حقیقی بہن اور ماں شریکی بہن پرورش کرنے میں دونوں برابر میں کسی کو کسی پر ترجیح نہیں ہے۔ پھر خالا نہیں پھوپھیوں پر مقدم ہیں۔ کیونکہ خالہ کو ماں کے ساتھ قرابت حاصل ہے نہ کہ پھوپھی کو ۔ اور پرورش کرنے میں مادری قرابتداری کو تر جیح ہے نہ کہ پدری قرابت کو پھر خالائیں درجہ بدرجہ اسی طرح رکھی جائیں گی جیسے ہم نے بہنوں کو بیان کیا۔ یعنی بچہ کی جو خالہ اس کی ماں کی حقیقی بہن ایک ماں باپ سے ہو وہ ادنی ہے۔ پھر اس کی ماں کی بہن جو ماں شریکی بہو پھر جو فقط باپ شریکی ہو۔ حاصل یہ کہ دو قرابت والی کو ایک قرابت والی پر ترجیح ہو گی ۔ پھر قرابت ام کو قرابت اب پر تر جیح ہو گی۔ پھر اسی طرح درجہ بدرجہ پھوپھیاں ہیں ۔ یعنی باپ کی حقیقی بہن مقدم ہے پھر باپ کی ماں شریکی بہن پھر باپ کی باپ شریکی بہن ہے۔
Chapter of custody... Explanation: The issue is that a woman who has two types of relationship is more entitled than one with one relationship. So it is said: the real sister, i.e., from both father and mother, is given priority over other sisters, i.e., only maternal half-sister and only paternal half-sister. Because the real sister has more relationship than those sisters, therefore she is given preference. Then the maternal half-sister is preferred over the paternal half-sister, because for sisters the right of custody is from the mother's side. For this reason the maternal half-sister is preferred over the paternal half-sister. Imam Zufar said: the real sister and maternal half-sister, in custody, both are equal; no one has preference over the other. Then maternal aunts are given priority over paternal aunts, because the maternal aunt has relationship with the mother, not the paternal aunt, and in custody maternal relationship is preferred, not paternal. Then maternal aunts are arranged degree by degree just as we explained for sisters: that the maternal aunt who is the real sister of the mother (from the same parents) is the highest; then the mother's sister who is maternal half-sister; then the one who is only paternal half-sister. The conclusion is that one with two relationships is given preference over one with one relationship; then maternal relationship is given preference over paternal relationship. Then similarly degree by degree are paternal aunts: i.e., the real sister of the father is given priority, then the father's maternal half-sister, then the father's paternal half-sister.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage explains the priority among women entitled to custody of a child in Hanafi law. The author begins by stating a general principle: a woman who has two ties of kinship to the child (through both parents) is more deserving than a woman with only one tie. The first illustration involves sisters: a real sister (full sister, sharing both mother and father) is preferred over both a maternal half-sister (same mother, different father) and a paternal half-sister (same father, different mother). This is because the real sister has a stronger blood connection. Next, the maternal half-sister is preferred over the paternal half-sister. The reasoning is that the right of custody for sisters derives from the mother's side, so maternal relationship is given precedence over paternal. Imam Zufar holds a different view: he equates the real sister and the maternal half-sister in custody rights. Then maternal aunts are preferred over paternal aunts, again because the maternal aunt is related through the mother, and maternal kinship is favored in custody matters. The same graded priority applies within aunts: within maternal aunts, the one who is a real sister of the mother (i.e., same parents) is highest, then the maternal half-sister of the mother (same mother), then the paternal half-sister of the mother (same father). Similarly, within paternal aunts, the real sister of the father comes first, then his maternal half-sister, then his paternal half-sister. The overall principle is that relationships with two linkages are superior to those with one, and maternal relations are superior to paternal ones in custody.

Key Terms
حقیقی بہن (haqīqī bahan): Real sister: a sister sharing both father and mother with the child.
ماں شریکی بہن (māṅ shārīkī bahan): Maternal half-sister: sister sharing only the same mother.
باپ شریکی بہن (bāp shārīkī bahan): Paternal half-sister: sister sharing only the same father.
خالہ (khālah): Maternal aunt: sister of the child's mother.
پھوپھی (phūphī): Paternal aunt: sister of the child's father.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which aunt has the highest priority for custody?
A) The maternal aunt who is a real sister of the mother
B) The maternal aunt who is a half-sister of the mother
C) The paternal aunt who is a real sister of the father
D) All aunts are equal

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi custody hierarchy prioritizes women with double kinship ties over single ties, and maternal relations over paternal relations, applied in a graded manner to sisters and aunts.

Loss and Return of Custody Due to Marriage
Rule on loss/return of custody due to marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on loss of custody due to marriage and apply the mahram exception to identify when custody is retained or regained.

Core Idea
Marriage to a non-mahram nullifies custody; the right returns when the marriage ends.

This passage addresses how a woman's marriage affects her right to custody (hadanah) of a child. The general rule is that any woman entitled to custody loses that right upon marriage to a man who is not a mahram relative of the child. However, if the husband is a mahram, the right remains because natural affection is presumed. Furthermore, the right is not permanently lost—it returns as soon as the marriage ends, since the obstacle (the non-mahram husband) is removed. The proof combines a Prophetic hadith and rational reasoning about the stepfather's likely lack of care.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Read the passage and find the statement that marriage of any custodial woman nullifies her right. Note the exception for a mahram husband.
The rule applies to all women entitled to custody: mother, grandmother, etc.
2
Understand the hadith proof
The author cites the hadith: 'You are more entitled to him as long as you do not marry.' This explicitly conditions the right on being unmarried.
The hadith is ahad (single-narrator) but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Recognize the mahram exception
If the husband is a mahram of the child (e.g., grandfather, uncle), the right does not fall because he will naturally care for the child. The grandmother's marriage to the grandfather is the key example.
Mahram means a relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited.
4
Understand return of right
When the marriage ends (by divorce or death), the woman regains her right at the original priority level.
The obstacle (non-mahram husband) is removed, so the right is restored.
5
Apply to the mother-grandmother example
The passage illustrates: mother marries stranger → her right falls → grandmother takes custody → mother divorces → mother's right returns and trumps grandmother's.
Priority of entitlement: mother first, then grandmother, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ان عورتوں کا حق حضانت کب ساقط ہوتا ہے
وكل من تزوجت من هؤلاء يسقط حقها لماروينا ولان زوج الام اذا كان اجنبيا يعطيه نزرا وينظر اليه شزر افلا نظر قال الا الجدة اذاكان زوجها الجدلانه قام مقام ابيه فينظر له و کذالک کل زوج هو ذو رحم محرم منه لقيام الشفقة نظرا الى القرابة القريبة ومن سقط حقها بالتزوج يعود اذا ارتفعت الزوجية لان المانع قد زال ترجمہ اور ان عورتوں میں سے ہر وہ عورت جس نے اپنا نکاح کر لیا ہو اس کا حق ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم روایت کر چکے۔ اور اس لئے کہ جب ماں کا شو ہر اجنبی ہے تو وہ اس کو حقیر چیز دے گا ۔ اور اس کو تیز نگاہ سے دیکھے گا۔ تو (بچہ کے حق میں ) کوئی نگہداشت نہیں ہے۔ سوائے نانی کے جبکہ اس کا شوہر ( بچہ کا ) دادا ہو۔ کیونکہ دادا بچہ کے باپ کے قائم مقام ہے۔ پس اس پر نظر شفقت رکھے گا ۔ اور یہی حال ہر ایسے شوہر کا ہے جو اس بچہ کا ذور تم محرم ہو۔ کیونکہ قرابت قریبہ کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے شفقت موجود ہے اور جس عورت کا حق پرورش نکاح کرنے کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو گیا۔ تو جب بھی زوجیت دور ہو جائے (اس کا حق پرورش ) لوٹ آئے گا کیونکہ مانع دور ہو گیا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جن عورتوں کو بچہ کی پرورش کرنے کا حق ہے۔ ان میں سے اگر کسی نے نکاح کر لیا تو اس کا حق پر ورش ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس کو سابق میں روایت کر چکے۔ یعنی حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے بچہ کی ماں سے فرمایا تھا انت احق به مالم تتزوجی تو بچہ کی زیادہ حقدار ہے۔ جب تک تو نکاح نہ کرے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس بچہ کی ماں کا شوہر جب اجنبی مرد ہے تو وہ اس بچہ کو تھوڑی چیز دے گا۔ اور تیز نگاہ سے دیکھے گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ ی شخص اس بچہ کی طرف کم التفات کرے گا۔ لہذا بچہ کو ان کی پرورش میں دینا اس کے حق میں کچھ نظر شفقت نہیں ہے۔ ہاں اگر اس بچہ کی نانی نے اپنا نکاح اس بچہ کے دادا سے کیا یا اس کی دادی نے اپنا نکاح بچہ کے نانا سے کیا تو اس نہانی یا دادی کا حق پرورش ساقط نہیں ہوگا۔
 Fr.
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد بهم یونکہ جدا ہوا اور نانا اس بچے کے باپ کے قائم مقام ہے۔ ہنڈا اس کی شفقت باقی رہے گی ۔ یہی حال ہر ایسے قوم کا ہے جو اس بچہ کا کے بندا گی۔ یہ کا نرم ہو، کیونکہ قرابت تقریبہ کی صرف نظر کرتے ہوئے شفقت باقی رہے گی۔ اور جس عورت کا حق پرورش کسی اجنبی مرد سے کہاں نے کی وجہ سے زائل ہو گیا تو جب بھی ان دونوں میں زوجیت دور ہو جائے تو اس کا حق پرورش اوٹ آوے گا۔ کیونکہ جو چیز روکنے والی تھی، و جاتی رہیں ۔ مثلا بچے کی ماں سب سے زیادہ حقدار ہے۔ لیکن اس نے کسی اجنبی مرد سے نکاح کر لیا حتی کہ ان کا حق زائل ہو میں سامر بچون پس پرس نانی زیادہ حقدار ہوگی ۔ لوک نانی نے اس کو اپنی پرورش میں لے لیا ۔ پھر چند روز کے بعد اس کی ماں گو اس کے شوہ نے طلاق دیقی ۔ غرض یہ کہ نگان زائل ہو سکیں۔ ہر ماں کا استحقاق بہ نسبت نانی کے مقدم ہو گیا۔
When does the right of custody fall from these women? And any woman from among them who marries, her right falls, due to what we have narrated, and because the husband of the mother, if he is a stranger (non-mahram), he gives her (the child) little and looks at her with harshness; is there not (lack of) care? He (the author) said: Except the grandmother when her husband is the grandfather, because he stands in the place of the child's father, so he will look upon him with affection. And likewise, any husband who is a mahram relative of the child, due to the existence of affection, considering close kinship. And the one whose right fell due to marriage, it returns when the marriage relationship ends, because the obstacle has been removed. Translation: And among these women, any woman who marries, her right falls, because of the hadith we have narrated, and because when the mother's husband is a stranger, he will give him (the child) insignificant things and look at him sharply, so there is no care (for the child) except the maternal grandmother when her husband is the child's grandfather, because the grandfather stands in the place of the child's father, so he will have affection. And this is the case for every husband who is a mahram relative of the child, because affection is present considering close kinship. And the woman whose right of custody fell due to marriage, then whenever the marriage relationship ends, her right returns because the obstacle has been removed. Explanation: The issue is that among the women who have the right to raise the child, if any of them marries, her right of custody falls. The proof is the hadith previously narrated: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to the mother: 'You are more entitled to him as long as you do not marry.' The second proof is that when the mother's husband is a stranger, he will give the child little and look sharply. So this person will pay little attention to the child, so giving the child to their care is not affectionate care. Yes, if the child's maternal grandmother marries the child's grandfather, or the paternal grandmother marries the child's maternal grandfather, then the grandmother's right does not fall because the grandfather stands in place of the child's father, so his affection remains. And the woman whose right fell due to marriage to a stranger, then whenever the marriage between them ends, her right returns because the obstacle is removed. For example, the child's mother is most entitled, but she married a stranger, so her right fell; then the maternal grandmother is most entitled and took the child. Then after some days, the mother's husband divorced her, so the marriage ended; then the mother's right becomes prior to the grandmother's.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of marriage on a woman's right to custody (hadanah) in Hanafi law. The author first states the general rule: any woman entitled to custody who marries a man who is not a mahram to the child loses her right. The proof is from two sources: (1) a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) told the mother, 'You are more entitled to the child as long as you do not marry'; (2) rational reasoning that a non-mahram stepfather will not treat the child kindly—he will give little and look harshly, so it is not in the child's interest to remain in that home. However, there is an exception: if the woman marries a man who is a mahram relative of the child, such as the grandmother marrying the grandfather, the right does not fall because the stepfather (the grandfather) is a mahram and will naturally have affection for the child, standing in place of the child's father. This exception applies to any husband who is a mahram (e.g., the child's uncle). Moreover, if a woman loses her right due to marriage, it returns as soon as the marriage ends, whether by divorce or death, because the obstacle (the non-mahram husband) is removed. The author gives an example: the mother is the most entitled, but she marries a stranger, so her right falls; then the grandmother takes custody. Later, when the mother divorces or the husband dies, the mother's right is restored and becomes stronger than the grandmother's. This illustrates the dynamic nature of custody rights based on changes in the family situation.

Key Terms
ساقط (sāqit): Fallen, nullified: the right of custody is removed due to a legal impediment (marriage).
محرم (mahram): A relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, allowing natural affection.
مانع (māni'): Obstacle or preventer: here, the presence of a non-mahram husband is a māni' that prevents the right from being exercised.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi law, when does a grandmother's right to custody NOT fall despite her marriage?
A) When she marries a stranger
B) When she marries the child's grandfather
C) When she marries any man
D) When she marries a wealthy man

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a woman's right to custody is lost upon marriage to a non-mahram but is fully restored when that marriage ends.

The Hanafi Order of Male Custodians When No Women Are Available
Determines male custody order when no female relatives exist

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy of male custodians ('asabah) for a child when no female relatives are available, and apply the principle of proximity to determine entitlement.

Core Idea
Custody goes to the nearest agnate ('asabah) — father, grandfather, brother, uncle, and so on.

This lesson unpacks the classical Hanafi ruling on male custody order when women are absent from the child's family. The source text establishes that the closest 'asabah relative has the strongest right, drawing from the known order of 'asabah in inheritance and marriage guardianship. Understanding this hierarchy is key to resolving custody disputes among male relatives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering condition
The rule applies when there is no woman from the child's family available for custody (hadanah). This includes all female relatives entitled to custody.
The absence of females triggers the consideration of males.
2
State the general principle
When males dispute custody, the most deserving is the one who is the closest in 'asabah (agnatic relation). The principle is that guardianship (wilayah) belongs to the nearest relative.
Proximity is measured by closeness in the agnate line.
3
List the order of 'asabah
The order is: father → grandfather (however high) → full brother → paternal half-brother → son of full brother → son of paternal half-brother → full paternal uncle → paternal half-uncle.
This order is derived from inheritance and marriage guardianship rules.
4
Consider the gender of the child
For a boy, maternal uncles and their sons may also be considered after the 'asabah order. Their order is: son of mother's full brother, then son of mother's paternal half-brother.
This is an expansion from the commentary.
5
Recognize the exception for girls
A young girl cannot be placed with a non-mahram 'asabah, such as a paternal cousin or mawla al-itaq. This exception will be covered in the next lesson.
The exception is based on avoiding fitnah.
