If there is no woman from the child's family for raising him, then which male is entitled to custody? If there is no woman from the child's family, and men dispute about his custody, then the most deserving among them is the one closest in 'asabah (agnatic relation), because guardianship (wilayah) belongs to the nearest, and the order of 'asabah is known in its place. However, a young girl is not given to a non-mahram 'asabah such as a mawla al-itaq (freed slave) or the son of a paternal uncle, to avoid fitnah. Translation: If there is no woman from the child's family to raise him, and men dispute, then the man most entitled is the one who is nearest in 'asabah, because guardianship is for the nearest relative, and the order of 'asabah is known in its place. But a young girl is not given to a non-mahram 'asabah, like the mawla al-itaq and the son of a paternal uncle, to avoid turmoil. Explanation: The issue is that if there is no woman from the child's family and men dispute about raising the child, then the most deserving is the one who is closest in 'asabah, because the right of guardianship belongs to the nearer relative. The order of 'asabah is known from its place, i.e., in the chapter of inheritance and marriage guardianship. The order is: father, then father's father (grandfather) however high, then full brother, then paternal half-brother, then son of full brother, then son of paternal half-brother, then the son who is the full brother of the father (i.e., paternal uncle), then the son who is the paternal half-brother of the father (i.e., paternal half-uncle). As for (the child's) maternal uncles and their children, a boy may be given to their care; the order is: first the son of the mother's full brother, then the son of the mother's paternal half-brother. A girl is not given to the care of the sons of her paternal uncles because they are non-mahram to her. If a girl has no 'asabah guardian, then she is given to the care of her maternal half-brother. If he is not present, then his son is the guardian. If not, then her guardian is the one who is her father's maternal half-brother. If not, then her guardian is her real maternal uncle, i.e., the real brother of her mother, then the maternal half-brother of her mother, then the maternal half-brother of her mother through mother. It is clear that the right of guardianship for non-'asabah relatives is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And since the mawla al-itaq (freed slave) is the last 'asabah, if there is no guardian, the girl is given to the care of the mawla al-itaq. Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage explains the rules for male custody (hadanah) when no female relatives are available. The author begins with the matn: if no woman exists among the child's relatives, and men dispute over custody, the most deserving is the one who is the closest agnate ('asabah). The principle is that guardianship (wilayah) follows proximity. The order of 'asabah is well-known from inheritance and marriage guardianship chapters: father, then grandfather, then full brother, then paternal half-brother, then sons of those brothers in order, then paternal uncles, etc. However, there is an important restriction: a girl (young female) cannot be placed under the care of a non-mahram 'asabah, such as a paternal cousin (ibn al-'amm) or a freed slave (mawla al-itaq), because of the risk of fitnah (moral harm). The commentary expands on this: if none of the 'asabah are available, then custody may go to maternal relatives according to Imam Abu Hanifa's view, which allows non-'asabah guardians to have custody. The order among maternal relatives for a girl is given: first her maternal half-brother, then his son, then her father's maternal half-brother, then her own maternal uncle (mother's full brother), then mother's paternal half-brother, then mother's maternal half-brother. If no suitable relative exists, the child goes to the mawla al-itaq (the former master who freed the child's ancestor), who is considered the last 'asabah. But again, for a girl, non-mahram relatives like the son of the paternal uncle or the mawla are excluded due to the lack of mahram relationship. The passage emphasizes that the welfare of the child, especially avoiding fitnah for girls, is paramount.

Key Terms
عصبہ (asabah): Agnatic relative: a male relative through the father's line (or female related through him) who inherits as residuary.
مولی عتاقہ (mawla al-itaq): The freed slave of a person; considered the last in the line of 'asabah for custody and inheritance when no other relative exists.
فتنہ (fitnah): Moral or social disturbance, including potential harm to a child's reputation or safety.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, which male relative is the first in the order of custody after the father?
A) Full brother
B) Paternal grandfather
C) Maternal uncle
D) Son of paternal uncle

Key Takeaway
The right to custody for male relatives follows the 'asabah hierarchy: the closest agnate is most entitled, but a girl may not be placed with a non-mahram male.

The Exception for Young Girls: Non-Mahram Prohibition and Maternal Custody
Explains the exception for girls and the alternative maternal custody order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which male relatives are prohibited from custody of a young girl due to non-mahram relationship, and list the alternative order of maternal relatives according to Imam Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
A girl may not be placed with a non-mahram male even if he is an 'asabah; custody shifts to maternal relatives or the mawla al-itaq.

The previous lesson established the 'asabah order for male custodians. This lesson focuses on a critical exception: when the child is a young girl, she cannot be given to a male custodian who is not her mahram, even if he is the closest agnate. The passage provides an alternative custody order through maternal relatives and explains the role of the mawla al-itaq as the last resort.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibition
A young girl (saghirah) is not given to a non-mahram 'asabah, such as a paternal cousin (ibn al-amm) or a freed slave (mawla al-itaq).
Non-mahram means a male with whom marriage is permissible.
2
Understand the rationale
The prohibition is to avoid fitnah (moral harm or social disturbance). Placing a girl alone with a non-mahram male may lead to inappropriate behavior or gossip.
Fitnah is a key consideration in family law.
3
List the alternative order for a girl
The passage gives the order: first, maternal half-brother; then his son; then the father's maternal half-brother; then the real maternal uncle (mother's full brother); then mother's paternal half-brother; then mother's maternal half-brother.
This order is based on Imam Abu Hanifa's view that non-'asabah relatives can have custody.
4
Note the role of mawla al-itaq
If no suitable relative exists, the mawla al-itaq (freed slave) is considered the last 'asabah and may take custody. However, for a girl, even the mawla is excluded if he is a non-mahram.
The mawla al-itaq is a residual heir in Hanafi law.
5
Distinguish between boy and girl
For a boy, maternal uncles' sons are acceptable; for a girl, they are excluded because they are non-mahram. The same applies to paternal cousins and the mawla.
Gender matters in determining mahram status.

Custody Order Among Male Relatives When No Female Is Available
Specifies entitlement to custody among male asabah and exceptions for girls

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the order of asabah for custody and identify the exception that prevents a girl from being placed with a non-mahram male relative.

Core Idea
Custody among male relatives follows the asabah order, but a girl must never be given to a non-mahram asabah.

When no female relative is available to care for a child, custody may be claimed by male relatives. The Hanafi school establishes a clear order of entitlement based on the closeness of agnatic relation (asabah), mirroring the order in inheritance and marriage guardianship. However, a critical exception protects young girls from fitnah: they cannot be placed with any male relative who is not mahram, even if he is an asabah. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proof, and an important intra-Hanafi difference regarding non-asabah relatives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and general rule
Recognize that the ruling applies when no female relative from the child's family exists. The general rule is that the closest asabah (agnatic male relative) is entitled to custody.
The text states 'فاولاهم اقربهم تعصيبا' — the most entitled is the nearest in asabah.
2
Apply the order of asabah
List the asabah in descending order: father, grandfather, full brother, consanguine brother, son of full brother, son of consanguine brother, full paternal uncle, consanguine paternal uncle, and so on. This order is well-known from inheritance and marriage guardianship.
The commentary provides the exact sequence: 'باپ پھر دادا پھر دادا اگر چہ اس سے بھی اوپر ہو۔ پھر حقیقی بھائی...'
3
Apply the exception for a girl child
If the child is a girl, she cannot be given to a non-mahram asabah, such as a paternal uncle's son or a freed slave (mawla al-'itaqah). The reason is to avoid fitnah (temptation).
The text says 'غيران الصغيرة لاتدفع إلى عصبة غير محرم' — only mahram asabah may take custody of a girl.
4
Consider the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on non-asabah
Imam Abu Hanifa extends the right of custody to non-asabah relatives (e.g., maternal uncle) in a specific order when no asabah exists. The Sahibayn restrict custody to asabah only.
The commentary notes 'غیر عصبات کے لئے ولایت کا حق امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے' — this is a valid ikhtilaf within the school.
5
Determine who prevails among several qualified males
If multiple brothers are equally asabah and mahram, the most righteous and pious is preferred. If equal in piety, the eldest has priority.
From the final paragraph of the commentary: 'اگر کسی بچہ کے چند بھائی ہیں تو ان میں جو سب سے زیادہ صالح اور متقی ہے...'

بچے کی پرورش کیلئے اس کے اہل میں سے کوئی عورت نہ ہو تو مردوں میں سے کون حضانت کا مستحق ہوتا ہے

لم تكن للصبى امرأة من اهله فاختصم فيه الرجال فاولاهم اقربهم تعصيبا لان الولاية للأقرب وقد عرف الترتيب في موضعه. غيران الصغيرة لاتدفع إلى عصبة غير محرم كمولى العناقة وابن العم تحرزا عن الفسة

ترجمہ: اگر بچوں کی پرورش کرنے والی اس کے کنبہ سے کوئی عورت نہ ہو۔ پس اس کی پرورش میں مردوں نے جھگڑا کیا ۔ تو ان مردوں میں سب سے زیادہ حق وہ مرد ہے جو عصبہ ہونے میں سب سے قریب ہو کیونکہ ولایت اقرب کے لئے ہے اور عصبات کی ترتیب اپنی جگہ پر معلوم ہو چکی، مگر یہ کہ صغیرہ کو غیر محرم عصبہ کو نہیں دی جائے گی ۔ جیسے مولیٰ عتاقہ اور (صغیرہ کے ) چچا کا بیٹا تاکہ فتنہ سے بچا جا سکے۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر بچہ کی پرورش کرنے والی اس کے خاندان اور کنبہ میں کوئی عورت نہ ہو پھر مردوں نے اس بچہ کی پرورش کرنے میں اختلاف کیا تو ان مردوں میں پرورش کرنے کا سب سے زیادہ مستحق وہ ہے جو عصبہ ہونے میں اس بچہ سے سب سے قریب ہو کیونکہ ولایت کا حق زیادہ قرابت والے کو ہوتا ہے۔ اور عصبات کی ترتیب اپنی جگہ معلوم ہو چکی ۔ یعنی باب میرات اور نکاح کرانے کی ولایت کے باب میں اور وہ ترتیب یہ ہے۔ باپ پھر دادا پھر دادا اگر چہ اس سے بھی اوپر ہو۔ پھر حقیقی بھائی پھر باپ شریک بھائی پھر حقیقی بھائی کا بیٹا پھر باپ شریک بھائی کا بیٹا پھر وہ چچا جو باپ کا حقیقی بھائی ہو پھر وہ چچا جو باپ کا باپ شریک بھائی ہو۔ اور رہی پھوپھی کی اولاد تو ان کی پرورش میں لڑکا دیا جا سکتا ہے اور ان میں ترتیب یہ ہو گی ۔ پہلے اس چچا کا بیٹا مستحق ہوگا جو اس بچہ کے باپ کا حقیقی بھائی ہے۔ پھر اس کا بیٹا جو اس بچہ کے باپ کا باپ شریک بھائی ہے۔ اور لڑکی اس کے چچا کی اولاد کی پرورش میں نہ دی جائے کیونکہ لڑکی کے پاس چچا کی اولاد اس کے غیر محرم ہیں۔

در اگر بچی کا کوئی ولی عصب نہ ہو تو اس بچی کو اس کے ماں شریک بھائی کی تربیت میں دے دیا جائے۔ اور اگر یہ بھی نہ ہو تو اس کا بیٹا ولی ہے۔ اور اگر یہ نہ ہو تو اس بچی کا ولی اس کا وہ چچا ہو گا جو اس کے باپ کا ماں شریک بھائی ہے۔ اور اگر یہ نہ ہو تو اس بچی کا ولی اس کا حقیقی ماموں ہوگا۔ یعنی اس بچی کی ماں کا حقیقی بھائی ہوگا۔ پھر اس بچی کی ماں کا باپ شریک بھائی پھر اس بچی کی ماں کا ماں شریک بھائی ۔ یہ واضح رہے کہ غیر عصبات کے لئے ولایت کا حق امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے۔ اور چونکہ مولیٰ عتاقہ آخری عصبہ ہے۔ اس لئے اگر کوئی ولی نہ ہو تو لڑکے کو مولیٰ عتاقہ کی تربیت میں دے دیا جائے گا۔ مگر لڑکی کو کسی عصبہ غیر محرم کی تربیت میں نہ دی جائے ۔ جیسے چچا کا بیٹا اور مولیٰ عناقہ کیونکہ اس میں فتنہ کا اندیشہ ہے۔

اور اگر کسی بچہ کے چند بھائی ہیں تو ان میں جو سب سے زیادہ صالح اور متقی ہے اس کو پرورش کرنے کا زیادہ حق ہوگا۔ اور اگر صلاح اور تقویٰ میں سب برابر ہوں تو ان میں عمر میں جو سب سے بڑا ہے وہ زیادہ حقدار ہوگا۔
For the upbringing of a child, if there is no woman from his family, then who among men is entitled to custody? ... If there is no woman for the child from his family, and men dispute over him, then the most entitled among them is the nearest in terms of asabah, because guardianship is for the nearest relative, and the order of asabah is known in its place. However, the young girl should not be given to a non-mahram asabah such as a freed slave (mawla al-'itaqah) and the paternal uncle's son, to avoid fitnah. ... Explanation: ...
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a ruling about custody when no female relative is available. The text first states the Arabic matn of Al-Hidayah, then provides Urdu translation and detailed commentary. The ruling is that among male relatives, the entitlement follows the order of asabah (agnatic heirs) as known from inheritance and marriage guardianship. The order is: father, grandfather, full brother, consanguine brother, son of full brother, son of consanguine brother, full paternal uncle, consanguine paternal uncle, etc. For a girl, there is an important exception: she cannot be given to a non-mahram asabah like a paternal uncle's son or a freed slave, due to fear of fitnah. If no asabah exists, the text mentions that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, non-asabah relatives (like maternal uncles) have guardianship rights in a specific order. The passage also addresses a situation where several brothers are equally qualified: the most righteous and pious is preferred, and if equal in piety, the eldest.

Key Terms
عصبہ (asabah): Agnatic male relative who inherits as a residuary
ولایت (wilayah): Guardianship or authority over the child
مولیٰ عتاقہ (mawla al-'itaqah): A freed slave who has wala' (patronage) over the manumitted person
فتنہ (fitnah): Temptation or moral corruption

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which male relative is first entitled to custody of a child when no female relative is available?
A) The maternal uncle
B) The paternal uncle
C) The father
D) The eldest brother

Key Takeaway
Custody among male relatives is determined by the order of asabah, but a girl must not be given to a non-mahram asabah to avoid fitnah.

Hanafi Refutation of the Child's Right to Choose in Custody
Hanafi refutation of Shafi'i view on child's choice in custody

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a child's choice in custody and evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal of the Shafi'i hadith evidence.

Core Idea
A child's immature judgment invalidates their choice in custody; only the Prophet's intercession made the hadith girl's choice correct.

In this lesson, we examine a key inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on whether a child who has reached the age of discretion can choose between parents in custody matters. The passage from Al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi argument that a child's deficient intellect makes their choice unreliable, and offers two responses to the Shafi'i hadith evidence. We will follow the structure of the dispute, analyze the evidence, and understand the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling of the Hanafi school: the child is not given a choice; custody is determined by the mother's right until a certain age (boys until independence, girls until marriage).
2
Identify the opponent and their evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a discerning child can choose between parents. Their key evidence is the hadith of the girl who chose her father after the Prophet's supplication.
3
Follow the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response has two parts: (1) the child's weak intellect leads him to choose comfort over welfare; (2) the Companions did not give choice. Then two responses to the hadith are given.
4
Analyze the rejection of the second response
The author of Al-Hidayah rejects the second response (that the hadith applies only to a mature child) because the hadith explicitly uses the word 'fateem' (weaned), indicating a young child.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in the Shafi'i school, a child's choice can transfer custody; in the Hanafi school, the mother's right remains regardless of the child's preference until the age limit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب حضانة الولد و من احق به
پس بچی اپنی ماں کی طرف مائل ہونے لگی۔ تو حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا اے اللہ اس کو ہدایت فرما پس وہ بچی اپنے باپ کی طرف مائل ہو گئی۔ اور اس نے اس بچی کو اپنی تربیت میں لے لیا۔ اس حدیث سے ظاہر ہوا کہ لڑکی اور لڑکے کو ماں باپ کے درمیان اختیار دیا جائے گا جس کو وہ پسند کریں وہ پرورش کرنے کا زیادہ حقدار ہوگا۔ (عنایه ) اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بچہ اپنی کم عقلی کی وجہ سے اس کو اختیار کرے گا۔ جس کے پاس اسے راحت ملے گی ، یعنی جو اس کو کھیل کے واسطے فارغ چھوڑ دے اس کو ترجیح دیگا۔ اور ظاہر ہے کہ ایسا کرنے میں نظر شفقت محقق نہیں ہوتا اس لئے بچہ کے اختیار کرنے پر پرورش کا حق نہیں دیا جائے گا اور یہ بات صحت کو پہنچ چکی ہے کہ صحابہ رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین نے بچہ کو مختار نہیں کیا۔ اور رہی وہ حدیث جس کو حضرت امام شافعی نے دلیل میں پیش کیا تو صاحب ہدایہ نے اس کے دو جواب دیئے ہیں۔ اول یہ کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی دعا سے اس بچہ کو اسی کے اختیار کرنے کی توفیق دی گئی جو اس کے لئے باعث شفقت تھا۔ اور ظاہر ہے کہ عام لوگوں کو حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم پر قیاس نہیں کیا جا سکتا۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس حدیث کو اس صورت پر محمول کیا جائے گا جبکہ بچہ بالغ ہو گیا ہو۔ صاحب ہدایہ کی طرف سے پیش کردہ دوسرا جواب قابل قبول نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ہم نے جو حدیث ذکر کی ہے اس میں وھی فطیم کی تفریح موجود ہے۔ اور تعلیم کہتے ہیں اس بچہ کو جس کا ابھی دودھ چھڑایا گیا ہو ۔ پس اس تصریح کے بعد حدیث کو بالغ ہونے کے بعد پر کیسے معمول کیا جا سکتا ہے۔
Chapter on custody of the child and who is more entitled to it. Then the girl began to incline towards her mother. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: O Allah, guide her. Then the girl inclined towards her father, and he took her into his care. This hadith shows that a girl and a boy will be given a choice between parents; whoever they prefer will be more entitled to raise them. (Inaya) And our proof is that the child, due to his weak intellect, will choose the one with whom he finds comfort, meaning the one who leaves him free to play. Obviously, such a choice does not ensure true compassion, so the right of custody is not given based on the child's choice. And it has been established that the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) did not give the child a choice. As for the hadith that Imam Shafi'i presented as evidence, the author of Hidayah gave two responses. First: Through the Prophet's supplication, the child was guided to choose what was better for him; obviously, ordinary people cannot be analogized to the Prophet. Second: This hadith should be interpreted as applying when the child has reached puberty. The second response presented by the author of Hidayah is not acceptable, because the hadith we have mentioned includes the phrase 'fateem' (weaned child). And 'fateem' refers to a child who has just been weaned. So after this explicit wording, how can the hadith be applied to a mature child?
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the right of a child to choose between parents in custody matters. The Shafi'i position, supported by a hadith of a young girl who chose her father after the Prophet's prayer, holds that a child who has reached the age of discretion can choose. The Hanafi school, as explained in this commentary, argues against this: a child's intellect is deficient, and he will choose based on immediate comfort (play, leniency) rather than true welfare. The Hanafis point out that the Companions did not give the child choice, and they offer two responses to the Shafi'i hadith: (1) the Prophet's specific intercession made the girl's choice correct, which is not generalizable; (2) the hadith might apply only to a child who has reached puberty. However, the commentator rejects the second response because the hadith explicitly mentions the child was 'fateem' (weaned), not baligh. Thus, the Hanafi position stands: a child below puberty has no choice in custody.

Key Terms
حضانة (ḥaḍāna): The right to physically care for and raise a child, including shelter, education, and daily supervision.
مختار (mukhtār): Given the right to choose between parents in custody disputes.
فطیم (faṭīm): A child who has just been weaned from breastfeeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, why is a child not given the right to choose between parents in custody?
A) Because the child's choice is always wrong and harmful.
B) Because the child's immature intellect leads him to choose based on comfort rather than true welfare, and the Companions did not give choice.
C) Because the mother has an absolute right to custody and no one can override it.
D) Because the father is always more entitled to custody regardless of the child's preference.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a child's preference does not determine custody; the mother's right takes precedence until the child reaches a specific age, due to the child's lack of mature judgment.

The Mother's Right to Relocate the Child: Conditions and Evidence
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for a mother to relocate her child after separation, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and cite the hadith proof.

Core Idea
A mother may move her child only to her hometown where the marriage took place—otherwise the father can demand return.

In Hanafi fiqh, custody (hadana) is the mother's right, but relocating the child after separation raises important questions about the father's access and the child's welfare. This lesson unpacks the precise ruling from Al-Hidayah: the mother may move the child only if both conditions—hometown and marriage location—are met. We'll also explore an internal Hanafi disagreement and the hadith evidence that settles the position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act and its category
The act is the mother's relocation of her child from the father's city to another city after separation (divorce). The ruling is about permissibility (jawaz) of this act.
This is not a pillar or condition of custody itself, but a separate ruling on movement.
2
State the two conditions
The mother may relocate the child only if (1) the destination is her hometown (watan), and (2) the marriage contract took place in that same town. Both must be present.
If the marriage occurred elsewhere, the father's implicit consent to reside there is not established.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
Two narrations from Imam Muhammad: Al-Mabsut denies the right without both conditions; Al-Jami' al-Saghir grants it based on the principle that contractual obligations bind at the place of contract.
The author prefers the Mabsut view as more correct (asahh).
4
Analyze the proof
The hadith 'Man ta'ahhala fi baladatin fa huwa min ahliha' (whoever marries in a city becomes one of its people) indicates that the husband has effectively consented to live there, supporting the mother's right to stay.
The hadith is cited from Ibn Abi Shayba via Uthman; it is ahad but relied upon.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that the mother may only move the child to her hometown where the marriage occurred. If the cities are close enough for daily visits, there is no objection.
Moving from village to city is allowed (child's benefit); city to village is not (harm).

Source Text

باب حضانة الولد و من احق به
۲۲۶
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم چاہا، حالانکہ وہیں نکاح واقع ہوا ہے۔ تو کتاب میں یہ اشارہ ہے کہ عورت کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے۔ اور یہ ( مبسوط ) کی کتاب الطلاق کی روایت ہے۔ اور حاصل یہ کہ جب مرد نے کسی عورت سے اس کے وطن میں نکاح کیا تو مرد بھی اس شہر کا باشندہ ہوگا اور عورت کا یہ شہر اس کا بھی وطن شمار ہوگا یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر کسی حربی کا فر نے دار الاسلام میں آکر زمیہ کا فرہ سے نکاح کر لیا، تو وہ ذمی قرار دیا جائے گا۔ صاحب نہایہ نے کہا کہ مصنف کا قول ولهذا يصير الحربي به ذمیاً کاتب کی غلطی ہے۔ اس لئے کہ ہدایہ کے علاوہ دوسری کتابوں میں یہ عبارت ہے ان المستامن اذا تزوج ذمية لا يصير ذميا لانه يمكنه ان يطلقها ويرجع يعنى جوهر بي دار الاسلام میں امن لیکر آیا۔ اور کسی ذمیہ سے نکاح کیا تو وہ ذمی نہیں ہو گا۔ کیونکہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ وہ طلاق دیکر واپس چلا جائے ۔ صاحب نہایہ مزید تائید میں فرماتے ہیں کہ میرے استاد نے خود فرمایا کہ شیخ مصنف کے نسخہ میں یہ عبارت نہیں ہے۔ اور غایہ البیان میں ہے کہ شیخ حافظ الدین الکبیر سے نقل کیا گیا کہ شیخ مصنف کے نسخہ سے مقابلہ کرنے میں یہ عبارت نہیں پائی گئی پس یہ کا تب کا سہو ہے۔ اور بعض حضرات نے حربی کی جگہ حربہ لکھا۔ یعنی اگر تر بیہ عورت نے دارالاسلام میں آکر کسی ذمی سے نکاح کیا۔ تو وہ زمیہ ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ شوہر اس کا دار الحرب جانے سے روکے گا۔ واللہ اعلم ۔ عینی شرح ہدایہ)
اور اگر عورت نے اپنے وطن کے علاوہ کسی دوسرے شہر میں بچہ کو لے جانا چاہا۔ حالانکہ وہیں نکاح واقع ہوا ہے تو کتاب یعنی قدوری میں اشارہ ہے کہ عورت کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے۔ اور یہ مبسوط کی کتاب الطلاق کی روایت ہے۔ اور جامع صغیر میں مذکور ہے کہ عورت کو اختیار حاصل ہے کیونکہ جس مقام میں عقد واقع ہو، تو عقد کے احکام بھی اسی مقام میں واجب ہوتے ہیں۔ جیسے بیچ جس جگہ واقع ہود میں طبیع سپرد کرنا واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اور عقد کا ایک حکم یہ بھی ہے کہ اولاد کو اپنے ساتھ رکھ کر پرورش کرے۔ اور اول یعنی مبسوط کی کتاب الطلاق کی روایت کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ نکاح کرنا جب پردیس میں واقع ہوا تو یہ عرف نہیں ہے کہ وہیں ٹھہر نا اپنے اوپر لازم کیا گیا۔ اور یہی روایت زیادہ صحیح ہے۔ اور حاصل یہ نکلا کہ عورت کو بچہ باہر لے جانے کے واسطے جب ہی اجازت ہوگی کہ دونوں باتیں پائی جائیں۔ ایک یہ کہ وہ عورت کا وطن ہو اور دوم یہ کہ وہیں نکاح پایا گیا ہو۔ اور یہ تفصیل اس وقت ہے جب دونوں کے درمیان اتنا تفاوت اور دوری ہو، کہ باپ اپنے بچہ کو دیکھ کر اپنے گھر رات نہیں گزار سکتا۔ اور اگر دونوں شہر ایسے نزدیک ہوں کہ باپ جب چاہے جا کر اپنے بچہ کو دیکھ کر واپس ہو کر رات اپنے گھر بسر کر سکتا ہے تو عورت کے لئے بچہ کو وہاں لے جانے میں کچھ مضائقہ نہیں اور یہی حکم دو گاؤں کے درمیان ہے۔ اور اگر عورت نے شہر کے گاؤں سے نکل کر شہر میں لے جانا چاہا تو کوئی مضائقہ نہیں۔
جامع صغیر میں مذکور ہے کہ عورت کو یہ اختیار ہے۔ کیونکہ عقد جس مقام میں پایا جائے اسی مقام میں عقد کے احکام واجب ہوتے ہیں ۔ جیسے بیع طبیع کے سپرد کرنے کو مکان بیچ میں واجب کرتی ہے اور منجملہ عقد کے احکام میں اولا دکوروکنے کا حق بھی ہے۔ اور اول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ پردیس میں نکاح کرنا عرفاً وہاں ٹھہرنے کو لازم کرنا نہیں ہے۔ اور یہی روایت اصح ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ دو باتوں کا جمع ہونا ضروری ہے۔ (۱) ون (۲) نکاح کا پایا جانا۔ اور یہ تمام تفصیلات اس وقت ہے جبکہ دو شہروں کے درمیان فاصلہ ہو۔ اور اگر ایسے قریب ہوں کہ باپ کے لئے ممکن ہے کہ وہ اپنے بچے کو دیکھ کر رات اپنے گھر گزارے تو اس بچہ کو لے جانے میں کچھ مضائقہ نہیں ۔ اور یہی حکم دو گاؤں کے درمیان ہے۔ اور اگر عورت شہر کے گاؤں سے نکل کر ) شہر کی طرف منتقل ہو گئی تو کچھ مضائقہ نہیں۔ کیونکہ اس میں بچہ کے حق میں بہتری ہے کہ شہر والوں کے اخلاق سیکھ جائے گا۔ اور اس میں باپ کا کوئی نقصان نہیں۔ اور اس کے برعکس کرنے میں بچہ کا ضرر ہے۔ اس لئے کہ بچہ گنواروں کے اخلاق سیکھے گا۔ تو عورت کو ایسا اختیار نہیں ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ عدت پوری ہونے کے بعد اگر مطلقہ عورت نے چاہا کہ اپنے بچہ کو اس شہر سے باہر لے جائے تو اسکو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ایسا کرنے میں باپ کو اپنے بچہ کی جدائی سے صدمہ ہوگا ۔ ہاں اگر عورت اس بچہ کو اپنے وطن لے جانا چاہے۔ درانحالیکہ شوہر نے اس عورت سے اس مقام میں نکاح کیا تھا۔ تو عورت کو اس کا اختیار ہے۔ صاحب عنایہ نے اس مسئلہ کی چار صورتیں ذکر کی ہیں ۔ اسلئے کہ عورت بچہ کو یا تو اپنے وطن لیکر جائے گی ، اور حال یہ کہ عقد نکاح بھی وہیں واقع ہوا ہے۔ یا اپنے وطن کے علاوہ لے کر جائے گی ۔ حالانکہ وہاں عقد نکاح بھی نہیں واقع ہوا ۔ یا عورت بچہ کو اپنے وطن لے جائے گی حالانکہ وہاں عقد واقع نہیں ہوا ہے۔ اور یا اپنے وطن کے علاوہ لے جائے گی ۔ اور و ہیں عقد واقع ہوا ہے۔ پس اگر دو باتیں جمع ہو جائیں وطن اور وجود عقد نکاح ۔ تو بچہ کو وہاں لے جانا جائز ہے ورنہ نہیں۔
جواز کی صورت میں دلیل یہ ہوگی کہ عورت کے وطن میں نکاح کرنے سے عرفاً اور شرعاً شوہر نے وہیں قیام کرنا اپنے اوپر لازم کر لیا تھا۔ عرفاً تو اسلئے کہ شوہر عادہ اس شہر میں قیام کرتا ہے جس میں نکاح کرتا ہے۔ اور شرعا اس لئے کہ حضور اقدس صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا: - مـن تـاهـل ببلدة فهو منهم يعنى جس مرد نے کسی شہر میں نکاح کیا۔ تو یہ بھی انھیں میں سے ہے۔ اور ابن ابی شیبہ نے اپنے مصنف میں حضرت عثمان سے روایت کی کہ انھوں نے منیٰ میں پوری چار رکعت پڑھیں۔ پھر فرمایا: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من تاهل في بلدة فهو من اهلها يصلى بصلاة المقيم وانى تاهلت مند قدمت مكة - يعنی رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ جس مرد نے کسی شہر میں نکاح کر لیا تو وہ اس شہر والوں میں سے ہو جاتا ہے کہ مقیم کی نماز پڑھے۔ اور جس وقت مکہ میں داخل ہوا تو میں نے ایک عورت سے نکاح کر لیا۔ اور ایک روایت میں ہے سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بقول من تاهل في بلدة فيصلى بصلاة المقیم نہیں۔ کیونکہ اس میں بچہ کے حق میں بہتری ہے کہ وہ شہر والوں کے اخلاق سیکھ جائے گا۔ اور اس میں باپ کے حق میں بھی کچھ ضرر نہیں۔ اور اگر اس کے برعکس اس نے شہر سے نکل کر گاؤں میں لے جانا چاہا تو بچہ کے حق میں ضرر ہے۔ کیونکہ گنواروں کے اخلاق سیکھے گا۔ لہذا عورت کو ایسا کرنے کا اختیار نہیں جمیل احمد سکروڈی۔
Chapter on the custody of the child and who is more entitled to it. ... (the passage details the ruling that a mother may only take the child to a place that is both her hometown and where the marriage occurred; otherwise she does not have this right. It includes an intra-Hanafi difference between the narration of al-Mabsut and al-Jami' al-Saghir, and provides a hadith proof from the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) narrated by Uthman.)
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya deals with the mother's right of custody and relocation of the child after separation. The author explains that the mother may move the child to a different location only under two conditions: (1) the location is her hometown, and (2) the marriage took place there. If both conditions are met, she has the right; otherwise, she does not. The text presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: the narration from al-Mabsut (and the indication from al-Quduri) denies the right if the marriage was not in the mother's hometown, while al-Jami' al-Saghir grants it based on the idea that contractual obligations are fulfilled at the place of contract. The author prefers the first view as more correct (asahh). The proof is a hadith from the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) that one who marries in a city becomes one of its inhabitants, implying the husband's consent to reside there. Additional details: if the cities are close such that the father can visit and return home the same day, there is no objection; moving from a village to a city is beneficial for the child and thus permissible, while moving from city to village is harmful and thus prohibited. The passage also includes a note about a scribal error in al-Hidayah regarding the ruling on a harbi becoming a dhimmi by marriage.

Key Terms
حضانة (hadana): Custody and upbringing of a young child, primarily the mother's right in Hanafi fiqh until a certain age.
وطن (watan): Hometown or domicile of the mother; a place where she is considered a resident.
عقد (aqd): Marriage contract (nikah); the legal agreement between husband and wife.
روایت (riwaya): A narration or transmission of a legal ruling from an imam, especially from Imam Muhammad's books.
عرف (urf): Custom or common practice; used as a secondary source of law in Hanafi fiqh when no explicit text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in this passage, under which conditions may a mother relocate her child to another city?
A) If the father agrees and the child is willing.
B) If the place is the mother's hometown and the marriage took place there.
C) If the new city has better schools and opportunities for the child.
D) If the mother has sole custody and can prove the father is unfit.

Key Takeaway
The mother's right to relocate the child requires both her hometown and marriage location; without both, she may not move, and the father can demand return.

Mother's Right to Breastfeed: Priority When Matching the Market Wage
States ruling that mother is more entitled to breastfeed for same wage or less than a stranger

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the mother's entitlement to breastfeed her child for wages and apply the verse 'La tudara' (2:233) to justify the limits on the father's obligation.

Core Idea
Mother's affection gives her priority, but she must accept the market rate; the father cannot be compelled to pay more.

In family law, breastfeeding rights can be contested. The Hanafi school balances the mother's natural affection with the father's financial responsibility. This passage from al-Hidayah explains that if the mother is willing to breastfeed for the same wage as a stranger, she is more entitled due to her compassion and the child's best interest. However, if she demands more, the father is not forced to pay—protecting him from harm as per the Qur'an.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The father refuses to hire the mother and brings a strange woman; the mother offers to breastfeed for the same wage as the stranger or for free.
2
State the ruling
The mother is more entitled (ahaqq) to breastfeed because she is more affectionate (ashfaq) and it is in the child's welfare.
3
Identify the condition
If the mother demands a wage higher than the stranger's, the father is not compelled; he may hire the stranger.
Condition: mother must match or accept lower wage to retain priority.
4
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quran 2:233: 'Do not harm a mother by her child nor a father by his child.'
5
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
Forcing the father to pay more than the market rate would cause him harm (darar), which is prohibited. Thus, the mother's right is limited to a fair wage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان قال الاب لا استاجرها وجاء بغيرها فرضيت الام بمثل اجرالا جنبية اورضيت بغير اجركانت هي احق لانها اشفق فكان نظر اللصبي في الدفع اليها وان التمست زيادة لم يجبر الزوج عليها دفعا للضررعنه واليه لاشارة بقوله تعالى و لا تضار والدة بولدها ولا مولودله بولدهای بالزامه لها اكثر من اجرة الاجنبية ترجمہ پھر اگر بچہ کے ) باپ نے کہا کہ میں بچہ کی ماں کو اجرت پر نہیں لوں گا ۔ ( بلکہ ) بچہ کی ماں کے علاوہ دوسری دودھ پلانے والی لایا۔ پھر اجنبیہ کی اجرت کے مثل پر (بچہ کی ماں راضی ہوگئی یا بغیر اجرت کے راضی ہوگئی تو یہی مستحق ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ یہ اپنے بچے پر زیادہ شفیق ہے۔ تو اس کو سپرد کرنے میں بچہ کے حق میں زیادہ بہتری ہے اور اگر بچہ کی ماں نے اجنبیہ کی اجرت سے یہ مانا تو شوہر زیادہ دیئے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ تا کہ اس سے ضرر دور ہو اور اسی طرف اللہ عزوجل نے ارشاد فرمایا ولا تـضــار والــدة بولدها ولا مولود له بولدہ یعنی ماں اپنے بچہ کی وجہ سے مضرت میں نہ ڈالی جائے گی اور نہ بچہ کا باپ اپنے بچہ کی وجہ سے ضر راٹھا دے گا۔ یعنی اس پر بچہ کی مان کے واسطے اجتہیہ کی اجرت سے زیادہ اجرت واجب نہ ہوگی۔
Then if the father said, 'I will not hire her,' and brought another (wet nurse). Then the mother agreed to the like of the wage of the stranger, or agreed without wage, then she is more entitled because she is more affectionate. So looking after the child (welfare) is in handing him over to her. And if she demands more, the husband will not be compelled to pay it, to prevent harm from him. And to this Allah Almighty pointed: 'Do not harm a mother by her child nor a father by his child' meaning the father is not obliged to pay more than the wage of a stranger.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where the father attempts to hire a strange woman to breastfeed his child instead of the child's own mother. The mother then steps forward and offers to breastfeed for the same wage that the stranger demands, or even for free. In this case, the mother has a superior right (ahaqq) to breastfeed her child. The reason given is that she is more compassionate (ashfaq) towards her child, and it is in the child's best interest to be with her. This is a form of parental preference based on the child's welfare (maslahah). However, if the mother demands more than the stranger's wage, the father is not forced to pay her more. That would cause him harm (darar), which is prohibited by the Qur'anic verse 'La tudaara walidatun biwaladiha wa la mauludun lahu biwaladihi' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:233). The verse is interpreted to mean that the mother should not be compelled to breastfeed against her will, nor should the father be forced to pay beyond what is reasonable. Thus, if the mother cannot be hired at a fair rate, the father may employ a stranger.

Key Terms
شفقت (shafaqat): Affection, compassion; the mother's natural affection for her child.
ضرر (darar): Harm; the principle that causing harm is prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the mother lose her priority to breastfeed her child for wages?
A) If she demands a wage higher than the stranger
B) If she agrees to the same wage
C) Only if she is a non-Muslim
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The mother's priority to breastfeed is conditional on accepting the market wage; the father cannot be forced to pay more due to the prohibition of harm.

Prohibition of Wasting Wealth and Ruling on Feeding Animals
Explaining the ruling on not feeding animals as wasting wealth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the prohibition of wasting wealth through neglecting to feed animals and explain the intra-madhhab dispute regarding compulsion.

Core Idea
Wasting wealth is haram, but sin and enforceability are distinct in Hanafi fiqh.

This passage addresses the Qur'anic prohibition of wasting wealth and applies it to the specific case of not feeding one's animals. The author demonstrates that neglecting to feed livestock constitutes a destruction of property, thus falling under the prohibition. However, an important intra-Hanafi dispute arises regarding whether the owner can be compelled by the state to feed them. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the evidence, and the preferred position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Not feeding one's animals is classified as wasting wealth (iḍā‘at al-māl). This is prohibited (haram) based on the clear hadith 'حرم عليكم اضاعة المال'.
The ruling applies to all owned animals.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith 'حرم عليكم اضاعة المال', which is a general prohibition of waste.
This is a textual proof (nass) from the Sunnah.
3
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf narrates that the owner should be compelled (majboor kiya jaye) to feed the animals. This view is also held by al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad.
The ikhtilaf is about legal enforceability, not the underlying sin.
4
Trace the tarjih
The author states that the correct (sahih) view is the first one: it is haram but without compulsion. This is the mufta bihi position.
Tarjih is based on the principle that compulsion requires a right of another, which is absent here.
5
Evaluate the thamarah
Practically, under the Hanafi mufta bihi, if an owner refuses to feed the animals, the court does not force him. He bears the sin, but no legal action is taken.
This distinguishes Hanafi fiqh from other schools on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حرم عليكم اضاعة المال اور ظاہر ہے کہ جانوروں کو چارہ نہ دینے میں اپنے مال کو برباد کر نالا زم آتا ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف سے یہ بھی روایت آئی ہے کہ مالک کو مجبور کیا جاے گلہ کہ جانوروں کو فقہ دے اور یہی قول امام شافعی ، امام مالک اور امام احمد رحیم اللہ کا ہے اور صحیح وہی ہے جو ہم اولا بیان کر چکے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
"Wasting wealth is forbidden upon you, and it is clear that not giving fodder to animals results in destroying one's wealth. And from Imam Abu Yusuf this narration has also come that the owner should be compelled to give fodder to the animals, and this is the saying of Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad (may Allah have mercy on them). And the correct is that which we have stated first. And Allah knows best what is correct."
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling regarding wasting wealth, specifically in the context of feeding animals. The author begins by citing the Qur'anic prohibition: 'Wasting wealth is forbidden upon you.' He then explains that not providing fodder to one's animals leads to the destruction of one's property, thus falling under this prohibition. The ruling is that it is haram (forbidden) to neglect feeding one's animals for this reason. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Yusuf is reported to have said that the owner should be compelled (majboor kiya jaye) to feed the animals. This view is also shared by the other major imams: al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad. However, the author declares that the correct position according to the Hanafi school is the first one—that it is forbidden but without compulsion. This means the act is sinful but not legally enforceable in court. The practical consequence: if an owner refuses to feed his animals, the court does not force him, but he bears the sin of wasting wealth. The author concludes with 'Allahu a'lam' affirming reliance on divine knowledge.

Key Terms
اضاعة المال (iḍā‘at al-māl): The act of wasting or destroying one's wealth without benefit, which is prohibited in the Quran.
مجبور کیا جاے (majboor kiya jaye): Being compelled or forced by legal authority to perform an action, here specifically to feed the animals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling regarding an owner who does not feed his animals?
A) He is compelled by the court to feed them.
B) It is haram but he is not compelled.
C) It is permissible as long as the animals survive.
D) He must sell the animals if he cannot feed them.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi holds that wasting wealth by not feeding animals is haram, but the owner is not legally compelled to feed them.

'Itq and Talaq: The Concept of Isqat in Hanafi Fiqh
Defines the book's subject and its relation to prior topics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why 'itq and talaq are both categorized as isqat and distinguish their respective effects in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Both emancipation and divorce nullify ownership, but one nullifies ownership of the entire person, the other only of marital intimacy.

The Hidayah commentary opens the Book of Emancipation by drawing a parallel between 'itq (emancipation) and talaq (divorce). Both are acts of nullification (isqat) that are irrevocable. Understanding this relationship helps situate 'itq within the broader Hanafi framework of legal nullifications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts of nullification
Recognize that the text compares 'itq and talaq as both being isqat.
2
Explain the object nullified in each
'Itq nullifies ownership of the slave's entire person (raqabah); talaq nullifies ownership of the right to marital intimacy (manfa'at al-buda').
3
List the other types of isqat
The text mentions ibra' (remission of debt) and 'afw (pardon for retaliation) as additional forms of isqat.
4
State why both are irrevocable
Emancipation and divorce, once executed, cannot be revoked, unlike other contracts.

ترجمہ (یہ) کتاب آزادی (کے احکام کے بیان میں ) ہے
تشریح آزادی اور طلاق کے درمیان مناسبت یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک اسقاط کے قبیل سے ہے ۔ مگر اتنی بات ہے کہ اعتاق ملک رقبہ کو ساقط کرتا ہے اور طلاق ملک منافع بضع کو ساقط کرتی ہے۔ دوسری مناسبت یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک میں لزوم ہے۔ چنانچہ جس طرح منق فتح کو قبول نہیں کرتا۔ اسی طرح طلاق بھی فتح کو قبول نہیں کرتی ۔ طلاق اگر چہ غیر مندوب ہے مگر اس کے باوجود مقدم کیا گیا تا کہ نکاح کے مقابلہ میں مذکور ہو جائے ۔ اسقاطات کی چند قسمیں ہیں ۔ پس اسقاط حق عن الرق عنق ہے اور اسقاط حق عن البضع طلاق ہے اور جو چیز کسی کے ذمہ میں ہو اس کو ساقط کرنا ابراہ ء ہے اور اسقاط حق عن القصاص والجراحات عفو ہے۔ حق (آزادی) مملوک کو حکما زندہ کرنا ہے۔ کیونکہ مملوک جمادات کے ساتھ ملحق ہوتا ہے۔ پس جب اس کو آزاد کر دیا تو کرامات بشریہ کا اہل ہو گیا۔ مثلاً آزادی کے بعد اس کی گواہی قبول ہوگی اور اس کو حق ولایت حاصل ہو گا اور آزادی کے بعد ان صفات کا حاصل ہونا جو آزادی سے پہلے حاصل نہیں تھیں ۔ در حقیقت اس کو زندگی عطاء کرتا ہے۔
لغت میں عشق کے معنی قوت کے ہیں عتق الفرخ اس وقت کہا جاتا ہے جبکہ پرندے کا بچہ طاقتور ہو کر اپنے پروں سے اڑنے لگے اور فرس عقیق اس گھوڑے کو کہتے ہیں جو دوڑ میں سب سے آگے نکل جائے اور ظاہر ہے یہ کام بغیر قوت اور طاقت کے نہیں ہو سکتا اور بیت عقیق کعبہ کو بھی اسی لیئے کہتے ہیں کہ وہ خدا داد قوت کی وجہ سے اپنے اوپر ہر حملہ آور اور مالکانہ قبضہ کرنے والے کو دفع کرتا ہے اور شریعت میں محقق اس شرعی قوت کو کہتے ہیں جس کی وجہ سے انسان شہادت ، ولایت اور قضاء کا اہل ہوگا۔ عتق آزادی، اعتماق آزاد کرنا معتق بکسر التاء آزاد کرنے والا معتق بفتح التاء آزاد کیا ہوا۔ پھر عشق کا سبب دو قسم پر ہے۔ اول یہ کہ آدمی کے ذمہ واجب ہو ۔ جیسے کفارہ ونذ روغیرہ میں آزاد کرنا واجب ہوتا ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ واجب نہ ہو تو اس میں ایک اختیاری ہے۔ دوم غیر اختیاری ہے۔ پس اختیاری یہ ہے کہ آدمی نے ثواب کی نیت سے کوئی غلام آزاد کیا اور غیر اختیاری یہ کہ اپنا قرابتی خریدا تو وہ اس کے مالک ہوتے ہی آزاد ہو جائے گا اور حق کی شرط یہ ہے کہ آزاد کرنے والا خود آزاد ہو اور عاقل بالغ ہو، اور مملوک کا مالک ہو خواہ مرد ہو یا عورت اور عشق کار کن وہ ہے جس سے آزادی ثابت ہو اور اس کا حکم رقیت اور ملک کا محل سے زائل ہونا ہے۔ پھر آزاد کرنے کے چند اقسام ہیں۔ اول مرسل یعنی فی الحال بغیر کسی شرط کے آزاد کر دیا۔ دوم معلق یعنی اگر تو ایسا کرے یا میں ایسا کروں تو تو آزاد ہے۔ سوم اپنی موت کے بعد آزادی کو منسوب کرنا پھر ان میں سے ہر ایک بعوض ہوگا یا بغیر عوض ۔ ( عنایہ، فتح القدیر)
This is the book of emancipation regarding its rulings. Explanation: The suitability between emancipation and divorce is that both are from the category of nullification (isqat). However, emancipation nullifies ownership of the slave's person (raqabah), while divorce nullifies ownership of the benefit of the private part (buda'). A second suitability is that both are irrevocable (luzum). Just as emancipation does not accept revocation, similarly divorce does not accept revocation. Although divorce is not recommended, it was placed before emancipation to be mentioned alongside marriage. There are several types of nullifications: nullification of the right over the neck (raqabah) is emancipation; nullification of the right over the private part is divorce; nullification of a debt in someone's liability is ibra'; and nullification of the right of retaliation and injuries is pardon ('afw). The right of emancipation is to give the slave life in a legal sense, because the slave is attached to inanimate objects. So when he is freed, he becomes eligible for human dignities; for example, after emancipation his testimony is accepted, he acquires the right of guardianship (wilayah), and he obtains qualities after emancipation that were not present before. In reality, it grants him life. Linguistically, 'itq means strength. It is said 'ataqa al-farkh when a bird's chick becomes strong and flies with its wings; a horse that outstrips others in a race is called faras 'atiq; and the Ka'bah is called Bayt 'Atiq because due to its God-given strength it repels every attacker and usurper. In the Shari'ah, 'itq is that legal strength by which a person becomes eligible for testimony, guardianship, and judgment. 'Itq is emancipation, i'taqa is to free, mu'tiq (with kasrah of ta) is the emancipator, mu'taq (with fathah of ta) is the freed person. The cause of emancipation is of two types: first, it is obligatory upon a person, such as freeing a slave for expiation (kaffarah), vow (nadhr), etc.; second, it is not obligatory, and this is further divided into voluntary (ikhtiyari) and involuntary (ghayr ikhtiyari). Voluntary is when a person frees a slave with the intention of reward; involuntary is when one buys a relative, who becomes free upon ownership. The conditions for emancipation are that the emancipator be free, sane, adult, and the owner of the slave, whether male or female. The effective cause (mujib) of emancipation is that by which freedom is established, and its ruling is the removal of slavery and ownership from the slave. Then the types of emancipation are: first, mursal (immediate) – freeing without any condition forthwith; second, mu'allaq (suspended) – if you do such-and-such or I do such-and-such, you are free; third, mudaf (deferred) – attributing freedom to after one's death. Then each of these may be with compensation ('iwad) or without compensation. (From Inayah, Fath al-Qadir).
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a definition-ruling type, introducing the entire Book of Emancipation (Kitab al-'Itaq) in the Hidayah commentary. The author begins by explaining the relationship between 'itaq (emancipation) and talaq (divorce): both are acts of nullification (isqat), but 'itaq nullifies ownership of the slave's entire person (raqabah), while talaq nullifies only the right to marital intimacy. Both are irrevocable. Then he lists different types of isqat: 'itaq, talaq, ibra' (remission of debt), and 'afw (pardon for retaliation). He explains that emancipation is like giving life to the slave, as it restores human legal capacity. The linguistic root of 'itq is 'strength' (quwwah), citing the example of a fledgling bird when it grows strong and flies, and the Ka'bah being called 'Atiq because of its strength against aggressors. Legally, 'itq is that strength which makes one eligible for testimony, guardianship, and adjudication. The causes of emancipation are divided into obligatory (e.g., for kaffarah or nadhr) and voluntary. Voluntary is further split into ikhtiyari (done for reward) and ghayr ikhtiyari (when a relative is bought and automatically freed). Conditions for a valid emancipation: the emancipator must be free, sane, adult, and the slave's owner. The types of emancipation are immediate (mursal), suspended on a condition (mu'allaq), and deferred until after death (mudaf), and each can be with or without compensation. The passage follows the order of first discussing the suitability of the book's placement, then definitions, causes, conditions, and categories, all in a single coherent unit.

Key Terms
عتق ('itq): Emancipation of a slave; legally, it is the removal of slavery (riqq) from the slave, restoring full legal capacity.
اسقاط (isqat): Nullification of a right or ownership.
طلاق (talaq): Divorce; nullification of the right to marital intimacy.
ابراء (ibra'): Remission of a debt or liability.
عفو ('afw): Pardon for retaliation or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a type of isqat mentioned in the passage?
A) 'Itq
B) Talaq
C) Ibra'
D) Bay' (sale)

Key Takeaway
Emancipation and divorce are both irrevocable nullifications, but they nullify different ownership rights.

The Hanafi Definition of 'Itq: Linguistic Roots and Legal Capacity
Defines 'itq linguistically and legally, and explains its effect on the slave's legal capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic root of 'itq (strength) and explain its legal meaning as restoration of full legal capacity.

Core Idea
Emancipation legally 'gives life' to the slave by restoring human dignities like testimony, guardianship, and judgment.

The text delves into the meaning of 'itq, first linguistically as 'strength' (quwwah), then legally as that which grants a person the eligibility for shahadah, wilayah, and qada. Understanding these definitions clarifies why emancipation is not merely a physical release but a legal rebirth.

Guided Path
1
Define 'itq linguistically
The text states that 'itq linguistically means strength (quwwah), illustrated by a bird's chick growing strong, a racehorse excelling, and the Ka'bah repelling attackers.
2
Define 'itq legally
In Shari'ah, 'itq is the legal strength by which a person becomes eligible for testimony, guardianship, and judgment.
3
Explain the effect of emancipation
Emancipation gives the slave life in a legal sense by removing him from the category of inanimate objects and granting him human dignities.
4
List the three restored capacities
The text specifies three: testimony (shahadah), guardianship (wilayah), and adjudication (qada).

In the Shari'ah, 'itq is that legal strength by which a person becomes eligible for testimony, guardianship, and judgment. 'Itq is emancipation, i'taqa is to free, mu'tiq (with kasrah of ta) is the emancipator, mu'taq (with fathah of ta) is the freed person. The cause of emancipation is of two types: first, it is obligatory upon a person, such as freeing a slave for expiation (kaffarah), vow (nadhr), etc.; second, it is not obligatory, and this is further divided into voluntary (ikhtiyari) and involuntary (ghayr ikhtiyari). Voluntary is when a person frees a slave with the intention of reward; involuntary is when one buys a relative, who becomes free upon ownership. The conditions for emancipation are that the emancipator be free, sane, adult, and the owner of the slave, whether male or female. The effective cause (mujib) of emancipation is that by which freedom is established, and its ruling is the removal of slavery and ownership from the slave. Then the types of emancipation are: first, mursal (immediate) – freeing without any condition forthwith; second, mu'allaq (suspended) – if you do such-and-such or I do such-and-such, you are free; third, mudaf (deferred) – attributing freedom to after one's death. Then each of these may be with compensation ('iwad) or without compensation. (From Inayah, Fath al-Qadir).
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a definition-ruling type, introducing the entire Book of Emancipation (Kitab al-'Itaq) in the Hidayah commentary. The author begins by explaining the relationship between 'itaq (emancipation) and talaq (divorce): both are acts of nullification (isqat), but 'itaq nullifies ownership of the slave's entire person (raqabah), while talaq nullifies only the right to marital intimacy. Both are irrevocable. Then he lists different types of isqat: 'itaq, talaq, ibra' (remission of debt), and 'afw (pardon for retaliation). He explains that emancipation is like giving life to the slave, as it restores human legal capacity. The linguistic root of 'itq is 'strength' (quwwah), citing the example of a fledgling bird when it grows strong and flies, and the Ka'bah being called 'Atiq because of its strength against aggressors. Legally, 'itq is that strength which makes one eligible for testimony, guardianship, and adjudication. The causes of emancipation are divided into obligatory (e.g., for kaffarah or nadhr) and voluntary. Voluntary is further split into ikhtiyari (done for reward) and ghayr ikhtiyari (when a relative is bought and automatically freed). Conditions for a valid emancipation: the emancipator must be free, sane, adult, and the slave's owner. The types of emancipation are immediate (mursal), suspended on a condition (mu'allaq), and deferred until after death (mudaf), and each can be with or without compensation. The passage follows the order of first discussing the suitability of the book's placement, then definitions, causes, conditions, and categories, all in a single coherent unit.

Key Terms
عتق ('itq): Emancipation of a slave; legally, it is the removal of slavery (riqq) from the slave, restoring full legal capacity.
معتق (بكسر التاء) (mu'tiq): The emancipator: the person who frees the slave.
معتق (بفتح التاء) (mu'taq): The emancipated slave: the person who is freed.

Causes, Conditions, and Types of Emancipation
Outlines the causes, conditions, and types of emancipation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the causes of emancipation, the conditions for the emancipator, and distinguish the three types (mursal, mu'allaq, mudaf).

Core Idea
Emancipation is either obligatory or voluntary; voluntary may be immediate, suspended, or deferred, and may be with or without compensation.

After defining 'itq, the text explains when emancipation becomes necessary (kaffarah, nadhr) and when it is voluntary. It also lays out the conditions the emancipator must meet and the different ways emancipation can be expressed: immediate, suspended on a condition, or deferred until after death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two primary causes of emancipation
The text divides causes into obligatory (e.g., kaffarah, nadhr) and non-obligatory (voluntary or involuntary).
2
List the conditions for the emancipator
The emancipator must be free, sane, adult, and the owner of the slave.
3
Define the three types of emancipation
Mursal (immediate, unconditional), mu'allaq (suspended on a condition), and mudaf (deferred to after death).
4
Explain the possibility of compensation
Each type may be with compensation ('iwad) or without, meaning the slave may pay for his freedom or be freed gratuitously.

لغت میں عشق کے معنی قوت کے ہیں عتق الفرخ اس وقت کہا جاتا ہے جبکہ پرندے کا بچہ طاقتور ہو کر اپنے پروں سے اڑنے لگے اور فرس عقیق اس گھوڑے کو کہتے ہیں جو دوڑ میں سب سے آگے نکل جائے اور ظاہر ہے یہ کام بغیر قوت اور طاقت کے نہیں ہو سکتا اور بیت عقیق کعبہ کو بھی اسی لیئے کہتے ہیں کہ وہ خدا داد قوت کی وجہ سے اپنے اوپر ہر حملہ آور اور مالکانہ قبضہ کرنے والے کو دفع کرتا ہے اور شریعت میں محقق اس شرعی قوت کو کہتے ہیں جس کی وجہ سے انسان شہادت ، ولایت اور قضاء کا اہل ہوگا۔ عتق آزادی، اعتماق آزاد کرنا معتق بکسر التاء آزاد کرنے والا معتق بفتح التاء آزاد کیا ہوا۔ پھر عشق کا سبب دو قسم پر ہے۔ اول یہ کہ آدمی کے ذمہ واجب ہو ۔ جیسے کفارہ ونذ روغیرہ میں آزاد کرنا واجب ہوتا ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ واجب نہ ہو تو اس میں ایک اختیاری ہے۔ دوم غیر اختیاری ہے۔ پس اختیاری یہ ہے کہ آدمی نے ثواب کی نیت سے کوئی غلام آزاد کیا اور غیر اختیاری یہ کہ اپنا قرابتی خریدا تو وہ اس کے مالک ہوتے ہی آزاد ہو جائے گا اور حق کی شرط یہ ہے کہ آزاد کرنے والا خود آزاد ہو اور عاقل بالغ ہو، اور مملوک کا مالک ہو خواہ مرد ہو یا عورت اور عشق کار کن وہ ہے جس سے آزادی ثابت ہو اور اس کا حکم رقیت اور ملک کا محل سے زائل ہونا ہے۔ پھر آزاد کرنے کے چند اقسام ہیں۔ اول مرسل یعنی فی الحال بغیر کسی شرط کے آزاد کر دیا۔ دوم معلق یعنی اگر تو ایسا کرے یا میں ایسا کروں تو تو آزاد ہے۔ سوم اپنی موت کے بعد آزادی کو منسوب کرنا پھر ان میں سے ہر ایک بعوض ہوگا یا بغیر عوض ۔ ( عنایہ، فتح القدیر)
This is the book of emancipation regarding its rulings. Explanation: The suitability between emancipation and divorce is that both are from the category of nullification (isqat). However, emancipation nullifies ownership of the slave's person (raqabah), while divorce nullifies ownership of the benefit of the private part (buda'). A second suitability is that both are irrevocable (luzum). Just as emancipation does not accept revocation, similarly divorce does not accept revocation. Although divorce is not recommended, it was placed before emancipation to be mentioned alongside marriage. There are several types of nullifications: nullification of the right over the neck (raqabah) is emancipation; nullification of the right over the private part is divorce; nullification of a debt in someone's liability is ibra'; and nullification of the right of retaliation and injuries is pardon ('afw). The right of emancipation is to give the slave life in a legal sense, because the slave is attached to inanimate objects. So when he is freed, he becomes eligible for human dignities; for example, after emancipation his testimony is accepted, he acquires the right of guardianship (wilayah), and he obtains qualities after emancipation that were not present before. In reality, it grants him life. Linguistically, 'itq means strength. It is said 'ataqa al-farkh when a bird's chick becomes strong and flies with its wings; a horse that outstrips others in a race is called faras 'atiq; and the Ka'bah is called Bayt 'Atiq because due to its God-given strength it repels every attacker and usurper. In the Shari'ah, 'itq is that legal strength by which a person becomes eligible for testimony, guardianship, and judgment. 'Itq is emancipation, i'taqa is to free, mu'tiq (with kasrah of ta) is the emancipator, mu'taq (with fathah of ta) is the freed person. The cause of emancipation is of two types: first, it is obligatory upon a person, such as freeing a slave for expiation (kaffarah), vow (nadhr), etc.; second, it is not obligatory, and this is further divided into voluntary (ikhtiyari) and involuntary (ghayr ikhtiyari). Voluntary is when a person frees a slave with the intention of reward; involuntary is when one buys a relative, who becomes free upon ownership. The conditions for emancipation are that the emancipator be free, sane, adult, and the owner of the slave, whether male or female. The effective cause (mujib) of emancipation is that by which freedom is established, and its ruling is the removal of slavery and ownership from the slave. Then the types of emancipation are: first, mursal (immediate) – freeing without any condition forthwith; second, mu'allaq (suspended) – if you do such-and-such or I do such-and-such, you are free; third, mudaf (deferred) – attributing freedom to after one's death. Then each of these may be with compensation ('iwad) or without compensation. (From Inayah, Fath al-Qadir).

Key Terms

معتق (بكسر التاء) (mu'tiq): The emancipator.
مرسل (mursal): Immediate emancipation without any condition.
معلق (mu'allaq): Suspended emancipation contingent upon a condition.
مضاف (mudaf): Deferred emancipation, typically after the death of the master.

Conditions for Valid Emancipation
Listing conditions and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for valid emancipation in the Hanafi school and explain why emancipating another's slave is valid (sahih) but not effective (nafidh) without the owner's permission.

Core Idea
Emancipation of another's slave is valid but ineffective without the owner's permission.

In this passage, we explore the four conditions required for a valid emancipation according to the Hanafi madhhab. The key distinction between validity (sihhah) and effectiveness (nafadh) is crucial: an act can be legally sound in itself yet not enforceable until a condition is met. We will also examine the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam Malik regarding a father's authority to emancipate his minor child's slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four conditions for valid emancipation
From the passage, list the four conditions stated by al-Quduri: the emancipator must be free, sane, adult, and the slave must be in his ownership.
2
Understand the rationale for each condition
The passage explains why each condition is necessary: a slave has no property, a minor lacks capacity, an insane person lacks capacity, and ownership is required based on the hadith.
3
Distinguish validity (sihhah) from effectiveness (nafadh)
The author of al-Hidayah clarifies that emancipating another's slave is valid (sahih) but not effective (nafidh) without the owner's permission. This distinction is central to the Hanafi position.
The passage explicitly says: 'emancipating an unowned slave is valid but its effectiveness is contingent upon the owner's permission.'
4
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam Malik holds that a father can emancipate his minor child's slave as an act of benefit. The Hanafi response argues that emancipation involves potential loss, so it is not an unqualified benefit, and the hadith prohibits emancipation without ownership.
The thamarah al-khilaf: according to Malik, the emancipation is effective; according to Hanafi, it is not effective without the child's later permission.
5
Apply the rulings to claims of minority or insanity
If a person claims they emancipated while a minor or insane, their statement is accepted because it denies validity. The passage explains the principle: the denier's word is taken.
This shows how the conditions affect evidentiary rules.

Source Text

حتی کہ اگر کسی نے دوسرے کا غلام آزاد کر دیا تو یہ نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ جمہور علماء کا یہی مذہب ہے۔ امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ اپنے نابالغ بچہ کے غلام کو آزاد کر سکتا ہے۔ مگر بالغ اولاد کے غلام کو آزاد کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ جمہور کے مذہب پر دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا فرمان لا عتق فيما لا يملكه ابن آدم ہے۔ یعنی جس کا آدم مالک نہ ہو اس کو آزاد کر نا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ اگر دوسرے کے غلام کو آزاد کیا تو یہ آزادی نافذ نہ ہوگی اور یہ نہیں کہا کہ صحیح نہیں ہو گی۔ اسلئے کہ غیر مملوک کو آزاد کرنا صحیح تو ہے مگر نفاذ مالک کی اجازت سے ہوگا۔ بغیر مالک کی اجازت کے نفاذ نہ ہوگا۔
And that the slave be in the ownership of the one who emancipates. So much so that if someone emancipates another's slave, it will not be effective. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'A person has no emancipation in what he does not own.' Explanation: In the text, 'ishq' (عشق) means emancipation (i'taq). Quduri stated four conditions for the validity of emancipation: First, the emancipator is free. Second, the emancipator is sane. Third, he is an adult. Fourth, the slave is in the ownership of the emancipator. Thus he said: Emancipation of a slave is not valid except from a free, sane, adult person, provided the slave is in his ownership. The emancipator being free is necessary because emancipation is only valid in one's own property, and one who is owned has no property. Therefore, an owned person cannot emancipate anyone. Adulthood is a condition because a minor does not have the capacity for emancipation, since emancipation apparently involves loss. For this reason, the guardian or executor of a minor is not permitted by Shari'ah to emancipate on behalf of the minor. The condition of sanity is imposed because an insane person has no capacity for any transaction. And since a minor is not capable of transactions, if an adult says, 'I emancipated this slave of mine while I was a minor,' his statement will be accepted and the slave will not be emancipated, because he has attributed the emancipation to a state (minority) that is contrary to the validity of emancipation. Thus this statement denies valid emancipation from him, and the statement of the denier is accepted. Therefore his statement will be accepted. And since sanity is a condition, if the emancipator says, 'I emancipated this slave while I was insane,' even if his insanity was apparent to people, his statement will be accepted. The proof is the same: he has attributed the emancipation to a state that is contrary to it. So he is a denier of emancipation, and the statement of the denier is accepted. Similarly, emancipation is not valid when a minor child says, 'Every owned person I own is free when I become an adult.' The proof is that a minor does not have the capacity to utter a statement that is binding upon him, because minors have been prohibited by Shari'ah from such statements. Then it is necessary that the slave he wishes to emancipate be in his ownership. So much so that if someone emancipates another's slave, it will not be effective. This is the madhhab of the majority of scholars. Imam Malik said: A person can emancipate the slave of his minor child, but cannot emancipate the slave of an adult child. The proof for the majority is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no emancipation in what the son of Adam does not own,' i.e., emancipating what one does not own is not valid. The author of al-Hidayah said: If someone emancipates another's slave, then the emancipation will not be effective, and he did not say that it is not valid, because emancipating an unowned slave is valid but its effectiveness is contingent upon the owner's permission. Without the owner's permission, it will not be effective.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute. It begins by establishing the fourth condition for valid emancipation: ownership. The Prophet (peace be upon him) is cited as proof: 'La 'itqa fi ma la yamlikuhu Ibn Adam' – no emancipation in what one does not own. The commentator then explains each of the four conditions from Quduri: the emancipator must be free, sane, adult, and the slave must be his property. The reasoning for each condition is given: a slave has no property, a minor lacks capacity (and his guardian cannot emancipate on his behalf because emancipation involves loss), and an insane person lacks legal capacity. The passage then discusses situations where a person claims emancipation occurred during minority or insanity – such claims are accepted because they negate the validity, and the denier's word is taken. It also rules that a minor's conditional declaration (all my slaves are free when I become adult) is invalid due to lack of capacity. Finally, it addresses the issue of emancipating another's slave: the majority (Hanafi) and Imam Malik's view. Imam Malik allows a father to emancipate his minor child's slave but not an adult child's. The Hanafi position is that such emancipation is valid (sahih) but not effective (nafidh) without the owner's permission. The author distinguishes between validity and effectiveness: the act is valid in itself but its enforcement depends on the owner's consent.

Key Terms
عتاق (itāq): Emancipation of a slave, setting free.
صحت (sihhah): Validity of the legal act in itself, as opposed to effectiveness (nafādh).
نفاذ (nafādh): Effectiveness; the legal act produces its intended consequences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what happens if a person says, 'I emancipated this slave while I was a minor'?
A) The slave is emancipated because the statement is explicit.
B) The statement is accepted and the slave remains enslaved.
C) The statement is rejected because it contradicts apparent age.
D) The slave becomes a mudabbir.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires four conditions for valid emancipation (free, sane, adult, ownership) and distinguishes between validity and effectiveness; emancipating another's slave is valid but not effective without the owner's permission.

Explicit Words for Emancipation in Hanafi Fiqh
Listing explicit words for emancipation with conditions and diyanah/qada ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the explicit words for emancipation according to the Hanafi school, explain why intention is not required for these words, and distinguish between the rulings diyānan and qaḍā'an when the master claims a different meaning.

Core Idea
Explicit words like 'Anta hurr' effect emancipation regardless of intention; the master's hidden intent is only accepted diyānan, not qaḍā'an.

This passage from Al-Hidayah lists the explicit (sarīh) words that immediately free a slave without the master's intention. It also addresses what happens if the master claims he meant something else. Understanding this distinction is crucial for knowing when emancipation is legally irrevocable in court versus private conscience.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a master uttering certain words to his slave. The ruling is that the slave becomes free immediately, regardless of the master's intention.
2
List the explicit words
From the text, identify the six Arabic phrases: 'Anta hurr', 'Anta mu'taq', 'Anta 'atiq', 'Anta muharrar', 'Qad harrartuka', 'Qad a'taqtuka'. These are sarīh (explicit) for emancipation.
These words are used exclusively or predominantly in Shari'ah and custom for emancipation.
3
Understand why intention is not needed
Because these words are explicit (sarīh), they do not require niyyah (intention). The text explains that although the words are grammatically khabar (news), they are treated as insha' (performative) in Shari'ah transactions by necessity, like divorce and sale.
The explicit meaning overrides any hidden intent.
4
Grasp the khabar-to-insha' transformation
Though these words are in the form of reporting, Shari'ah treats them as creative utterances that bring about the legal effect immediately. This is a pragmatic shift for legal certainty.
5
Apply the diyanah/qada distinction
If the master claims he meant 'false news' or 'free from work', he is believed diyānan (between him and Allah) because the words could bear that meaning. But he is not believed qaḍā'an (in court) because it contradicts the apparent meaning (zahir). Thus, the slave is freed legally.
Diyānan relates to inner truth; qaḍā'an to apparent evidence.

And if a master says to his male slave or female slave: 'Anta hurr', or 'Anta mu'taq', or 'Anta 'atiq', or 'Anta muharrar', or 'Qad harrartuka', or 'Qad a'taqtuka', then he becomes free, whether he intended emancipation by it or not. Because these words are explicit (sarīh) in it, as they are used in that meaning in Shari'ah and custom. So being explicit dispenses with the need for intention. And although the literal formulation (wad') of these words is in the form of khabar (news), they have been made insha' (creative) in Shari'ah transactions due to necessity, as in divorce and sale and others. And if he says, 'I intended by it false news' or 'that he is free from work', he is believed diyanatan (in conscience), because it is possible for the word, but he is not believed qada'an (in court), because it is against the apparent meaning. Translation: If a master says to his male slave or female slave: 'You are free', or 'mu'taq', or 'atiq', or 'muharrar', or 'I have freed you', or 'I have emancipated you', then he becomes free, whether he intended emancipation by that word or not. Because these words are explicit in the meaning of emancipation. They are used in that meaning in Shari'ah and custom. So being explicit dispenses with intention. And although these words are originally in the meaning of khabar (news), yet for necessity they have been made insha' in Shari'ah transactions, as in divorce and sale, etc. And if he says, 'I intended by these words false news' or 'that you are free from work', then he is believed diyanatan, because the word also bears that meaning, but he is not believed qada'an, because it is against the apparent meaning.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is a definition-ruling passage that lists explicit words for emancipation. It identifies six Arabic expressions that are sarīh (explicit) in effecting emancipation, meaning they create the legal effect without needing to ascertain intention. These are: 'Anta hurr' (you are free), 'Anta mu'taq' (you are emancipated), 'Anta 'atiq' (you are freed), 'Anta muharrar' (you are liberated), 'Qad harrartuka' (I have freed you), and 'Qad a'taqtuka' (I have emancipated you). Because these words are used exclusively or predominantly in Shari'ah and custom for emancipation, they are considered explicit, and thus niyyah (intention) is not required. The text explains that although these words are grammatically in the form of khabar (informative statements), in Shari'ah transactions they are treated as insha' (performative utterances) due to necessity – similar to divorce (talaq) and sale (bay'). The passage then addresses a scenario where the master claims he intended something else, such as false news (khabar al-batil) or meaning 'free from work'. In such a case, according to the distinction between diyanah (conscience) and qada' (judicial ruling), the master is believed in his private conscience because the words could bear those meanings, but in court his claim is not accepted because it contradicts the apparent meaning (zahir) which is emancipation. Thus, the slave is freed legally despite the master's inner intention.

Key Terms
صريح (sarīh): Explicit wording that clearly indicates emancipation without needing intention or context.
ديانة (diyānah): In conscience, between the person and Allah; a claim accepted privately but not in court.
قضاء (qaḍā'an): Judicially, in court; based on apparent evidence, not inner intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The slave is free because the words are explicit.
B) The slave is not free because of the master's intention.
C) The slave becomes a mudabbir.
D) The slave is free only if witnesses are present.

Key Takeaway
Explicit words of emancipation (Anta hurr, etc.) make the slave free immediately; the master's hidden intention is only relevant diyānan, not qaḍā'an.
